- **The show-card Play button now continues *forward* from the last episode you watched instead of jumping back to one you skipped.** Within a multi-episode item (e.g. a season pack), if you skipped ep5 and watched ep6 partway, Play correctly resumes ep6 — but once ep6 was *finished*, the resume hint walked the file list from the start and offered ep5 (the first not-completed file) again, instead of advancing to ep7. `find_resume_hint` now scans **from the last-watched file onward** first: it resumes an in-progress `last_file`, else returns the first not-completed episode at/after it (skipping `last_file` only when completed), so finishing ep6 advances to ep7. It only falls back to the global "first un-watched anywhere" walk when nothing ahead is left (which still surfaces a genuinely-skipped earlier gap once the rest of the series is done, and remains the cold-start path). **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`find_resume_hint`). **Docs:** [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.32.0] — 2026-06-14
- **Smart Skip no longer cuts off the end of a show by guessing at credits.** Credit detection sometimes triggered early — on an episode whose usual end-credits sequence was absent or shorter, the audio-fingerprint matcher latched onto the only *other* recurring audio it could find (a stinger/repeated gag) and auto-skip then advanced there, losing the actual ending. Credits time now comes **only** from a confirmed cross-episode fingerprint match, with **no fabricated fallback**: the old flat-`duration×0.92` guess and the black-frame detector are both **removed**. A matched outro run is accepted only when it **starts late enough** (`≥ duration × MIN_CREDITS_PCT`, 0.75) **and runs to ~the end of the file** (`credits_end ≥ duration − OUTRO_END_MARGIN_SEC`, 120 s) — real credits reach the end, a recurring mid/late cue is followed by more content and is rejected. A new consensus pass (`_filter_cluster_consensus`) prunes a cluster member that matched the season on a *different* region than the real credits (anchor-offset deviation > `CLUSTER_OFFSET_TOL_FRAMES`, ~8 s), applied to both intros and outros. Alternate credits shared by **multiple** episodes are still detected (they form their own cluster); an episode with no genuine match — or a single file with no peer episodes — now gets **no** skip (a `no_skip_points` "Skip unavailable" state) rather than an early guess. `ANALYZER_VERSION` is bumped 3 → 4, so every already-processed series is **re-analyzed automatically** by the idle maintenance loop / next prep (manual admin edits are untouched). **Analyzer:** [analyzer.py](analyzer.py) (`_filter_cluster_consensus`, fingerprint-only credits acceptance in `analyze_series`, removed `_detect_blackframe`/`CREDITS_FALLBACK_PCT`/`ERR_TOO_SHORT`, new `MIN_CREDITS_PCT`/`OUTRO_END_MARGIN_SEC`/`CLUSTER_OFFSET_TOL_FRAMES`, `ANALYZER_VERSION = 4`). **Docs:** [docs/ANALYZER.md](docs/ANALYZER.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md), [docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md](docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md), [docs/ARCHITECTURE.md](docs/ARCHITECTURE.md).

## [5.31.1] — 2026-06-14
- **Fixed search still failing (and showing no results) when only *some* indexers are broken.** The 5.31.0 partial-failure handling read Jackett's per-indexer error block but still issued one request to the aggregate `/indexers/all/results` endpoint — and that endpoint waits for the *slowest* indexer, so a single hung/broken one blew our client timeout and the `502` discarded **every** result, including the good ones. `/api/search` now enumerates the configured indexers (`_list_configured_indexers`) and queries each **independently and concurrently** (`/indexers/{id}/results`, 12 s per-indexer timeout); a failing indexer only loses its own results and we merge + return whatever came back. It only surfaces an error when **every** indexer fails. Falls back to the aggregate endpoint if the indexer list can't be fetched. Health is now built from the live per-indexer query outcomes via the shared `_apply_indexer_health`.
- **Fixed the admin "Open Jackett Admin" link pointing at `http://localhost:9117`** — useless from a remote browser, where "localhost" is the admin's own machine. `_jackett_dashboard_url(request)` now swaps the loopback host for the hostname the admin actually connected on (keeping Jackett's scheme + port); a non-loopback `INDEXER_URL` (remote Jackett) is left as-is.
- **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`_apply_indexer_health`, `_record_indexer_health`, `_list_configured_indexers`, `_shape_search_results`, rewritten `/api/search`, `_jackett_dashboard_url(request)` + callers). **Docs:** [docs/API.md](docs/API.md).

## [5.31.0] — 2026-06-14
- **Search now survives a single broken indexer — and flags it instead of failing.** Jackett's aggregate `/indexers/all/results` endpoint already returns results from the indexers that *did* respond and reports the ones that errored in its `Indexers` block, but the search endpoint ignored that block, so a degraded fan-out was invisible. `/api/search` now reads it (`_record_indexer_health`): as long as at least one indexer answers, the search bar keeps working, and when *some* fail while others succeed it raises a **non-specific** degraded flag — never naming which indexers are down. The dashboard shows a quiet amber banner ("Some search sources aren't responding — results may be incomplete.") driven by the new `indexers_degraded` / `indexers_total` / `indexers_failing` state fields (`state_snapshot`, surfaced in `renderServerAttention`). The admin **Indexers** tab gains an **Indexer Health** card: a per-indexer Responding/Failing list (with the failure reason), **Test** (per indexer) and **Test All** buttons that probe Jackett's per-indexer test endpoint live, a degraded/all-OK summary banner, and an **Open Jackett Admin ↗** link to the Jackett dashboard so the admin can log in and fix or remove the failing indexers directly. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`AppState.indexers_degraded`/`indexers_total`/`indexers_failing`/`indexer_health`, `state_snapshot`, `_record_indexer_health`, `/api/search`, `GET /api/admin/indexers/health`, `POST /api/admin/indexers/{id}/test`, `POST /api/admin/indexers/test-all`, `_jackett_dashboard_url`). **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`renderServerAttention` indexer-degraded branch), [static/admin.html](static/admin.html) (Indexer Health card, `loadIndexerHealth`/`testAllIndexers`/`testOneIndexer`/`_renderIndexerHealth`). **Docs:** [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md).

## [5.30.1] — 2026-06-13
- **Fixed the indexer (Jackett) intermittently going "unreachable" for searches until you retried several times.** The watchdog declared Jackett down and force-killed it (then sat through a ~40 s mono/.NET cold restart) on a **single** failed HTTP health probe. Jackett's web stack can briefly stop answering `/UI/Login` within the probe timeout while it's busy — fanning a search out to every indexer, or under CPU load from the idle auto-fingerprint/auto-validate maintenance added in 5.21.0 — so a transient slow response was repeatedly cold-restarting the indexer mid-search, surfacing as `502 Indexer unreachable` that "eventually works." The watchdog now tolerates consecutive failed probes before the destructive restart (`ServiceSpec.failure_grace`; Jackett = 2, so ~1 min of *sustained* failure is still recovered, mirroring the in-app `jackett_health_monitor` backstop) and the per-probe timeout is bumped 4 s → 6 s. Port-checked services (VLC, qBit) keep `grace=0` so crash recovery stays immediate. **Watchdog:** [watchdog.py](watchdog.py) (`ServiceSpec.failure_grace`/`_health_misses`, plain-service loop grace logic, `_jackett_alive` timeout). **Docs:** [docs/DAEMON_WATCHDOG.md](docs/DAEMON_WATCHDOG.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.30.0] — 2026-06-13
- **New "Use My Computer" control in Profile Settings — pause the background video and stop VLC grabbing the screen / minimizing your windows so you can use the machine normally.** The host normally runs an idle background video that re-fullscreens VLC and minimizes every other window (`background_video_loop` + `vlc_focus_and_fullscreen`/`_minimize_other_windows_windows`), which fights a user trying to use the same computer. Profile Settings → **Global** now has a **Use My Computer** tile with three buttons — **60 Sec**, **2 Min**, and **Until I Stop** — that pause all of it; while paused the tile shows a live "Paused — resumes in m:ss" (or "until you resume") line with a **Resume** button. A single server-side gate, `window_mgmt_paused()` ([main.py](main.py)), backs it: `vlc_focus_and_fullscreen` returns immediately and `background_video_loop` skips (re)starting the idle video while paused, so every focus/minimize/fullscreen assertion stands down. Pausing also minimizes VLC right away (`vlc_minimize`) so the desktop is usable instantly instead of waiting for the current background video to end; resuming kicks `vlc_focus_and_fullscreen` so the background video returns to the foreground without waiting for the 3 s poll. A timed pause auto-expires server-side on read and the UI counts it down locally between SSE state events. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`AppState.window_mgmt_paused_until`, `window_mgmt_paused()`, guards in `vlc_focus_and_fullscreen`/`background_video_loop`, `state_snapshot` `window_mgmt_paused`/`window_mgmt_pause_remaining`, `WindowControlReq`, `POST /api/window-control`). **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`#wcButtons`/`#wcResume` tile, `pauseWindowControl`/`resumeWindowControl`/`renderWindowControl`, SSE `state` + `openProfileSettings`/`closeProfileSettings` hooks). **Docs:** [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/BACKEND.md](docs/BACKEND.md), [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md).

## [5.29.0] — 2026-06-12
- **New Dev Mode setting — a live diagnostics overlay for on-device streaming.** Profile Settings gains a **This Device** section (settings stored in the browser's localStorage, not on the server — these stats are properties of the viewing device, not the host or profile) with a **Dev Mode** toggle. While on, the on-device player shows a pointer-through monospace HUD (`#lpDevHud`, top-left under the header) repainted at 1 Hz with the streaming internals: playback engine + mode (hls.js/native · bundle/on-demand, plus a RECONNECTING flag while the network-retry loop runs), the **quality rung actually playing** (height + bitrate, auto vs. pinned, from `lp.hls.levels`), the hls.js **bandwidth estimate**, the **last segment's download speed** (size/duration/rate from `FRAG_LOADED` stats, recorded only while Dev Mode is on), the decoded video dimensions, **how far ahead playback has buffered** (seconds past the playhead + buffered-range count), dropped/total frames (`getVideoPlaybackQuality`), and a session stall counter + `readyState`. The HUD deliberately ignores the controls' auto-hide (it exists to be watched), hides in tiny-tile mode, toggles live mid-playback, and costs nothing while off (no interval, no stat collection). Safari-native HLS exposes no level/bandwidth API, so there the HUD shows decode size/buffer/frames only. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`#psDevMode` + This Device section, `toggleDevMode`, `devMode` localStorage flag, `#lpDevHud` + CSS, `_lpDevHudStart`/`_lpDevHudStop`/`_lpDevHudTick`/`_lpDevNoteFrag`/`_lpDevFmtBits`, hooks in `lpPlay`/`lpStop`/`FRAG_LOADED`/`waiting`). **Docs:** [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md).

## [5.28.1] — 2026-06-12
- **Fixed the on-device player's forward buffer being capped at ~30 s on Safari (macOS and iOS) instead of the intended ~3 minutes.** Safari 17.1+ exposes the new ManagedMediaSource API — on macOS *alongside* classic MediaSource — and hls.js 1.5 prefers MMS by default (`preferManagedMediaSource: true`). Under MMS the OS owns the fetch cadence: it stops segment loading once ~30 s is buffered and duty-cycles the radio (buffer drains to ~10–15 s, then refills), silently defeating the `maxBufferLength: 180` outage buffer added in 5.24.0. The player now passes `preferManagedMediaSource: false`, so every browser with classic MSE (macOS Safari, Chrome, Firefox, Edge) gets the full 3-minute buffer again. On iOS classic MSE doesn't exist, so hls.js still falls back to MMS there — the ~30 s ceiling on iPhone is an OS-level battery optimization that cannot be lifted (documented as a platform gap). **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (hls.js config). **Docs:** [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.28.0] — 2026-06-12
- **On-device player: new orientation-lock button — keep watching in landscape even when the phone auto-rotates to portrait.** A new rotate-lock button (`#lpRotBtn`, touch devices only — hidden on fine pointers) in the bottom control strip toggles `.lp-lock-landscape` on `#localPlayer`. Two mechanisms cooperate: where the Screen Orientation API works (Android, in OS fullscreen) `screen.orientation.lock("landscape")` pins the real viewport; everywhere else — iPhone Safari has no lock API at all — a CSS fallback fires whenever the viewport goes portrait, rotating the entire player 90° (`@media (orientation:portrait)`: sized to the swapped viewport dimensions `100dvh`×`100dvw`, centered, `rotate(90deg)`), so the video **and the custom controls** keep rendering landscape no matter how the phone is held. The two paths can't conflict: when the native lock holds, the portrait media query never matches. Browser hit-testing follows the CSS transform automatically; the one manual fix is the seek bar's scrub math (`_lpSeekPosFromEvent` scrubs along `clientY` while rotated, via the new `_lpRotated()` helper). The lock clears itself on stop and on minimize-to-tile (`_lpClearOrientLock` — a rotated corner tile would be absurd), and the button tints indigo while engaged. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`#lpRotBtn`, `.lp-lock-landscape` CSS, `lpToggleOrientLock`/`_lpClearOrientLock`/`_lpRotated`, `_lpSeekPosFromEvent`, cleanup in `lpStop`/`lpMinimize`). **Docs:** [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.27.0] — 2026-06-12
- **Fixed the mobile UI feeling "loose" — overscrolling in the wrong place could rubber-band, shift, or break the layout — and gave the on-device player true fullscreen on iPhone Safari.** The document body was the page's scroll container while the header was `sticky` and every panel (episode page, players, modals) a `fixed` overlay — so on phones, any overscroll rubber-banded the *entire page*: fixed footers/overlays visibly detached, pull-to-refresh fired mid-scroll, and flicking past the end of a modal list scrolled the page hiding underneath. The dashboard is now a **height-locked app shell**: `html`/`body` are `100dvh` + `overflow:hidden` with `overscroll-behavior:none` (the body intentionally drops `min-h-screen` — `100vh` overshoots `100dvh` while the mobile URL bar is visible), making `<main>` and the overlay lists the only things that can scroll. Every scrollable region gets `overscroll-behavior:contain` so its momentum never chains to whatever is behind it, horizontal strips (season tabs) get `overscroll-behavior-x:contain` so a hard flick can't trigger browser back/forward swipe, and `touch-action:manipulation` on the shell kills accidental double-tap zoom (pinch-zoom still works). No JS read `window.scrollY` or used window scroll listeners, so nothing else changes. **True fullscreen on iPhone:** the player's fullscreen button — previously hidden on iPhone Safari (no element-fullscreen API) — now falls back to the `<video>`'s native `webkitEnterFullscreen()`: genuinely full screen (no browser chrome at all), native transport while fullscreen, in-stream audio/sub tracks still work (they're in the HLS manifest on the Safari-native path), and `webkitendfullscreen` resyncs the custom UI on exit. **Swipe-to-minimize the browser bar** also still works during playback: a locked document means the browser can never auto-hide its URL bar (that only happens on real *root* scrolls), so while `#localPlayer` is open full-screen (not the tiny tile) an `html:has(...)` rule (coarse-pointer only) re-enables root scrolling by making `<body>` 45vh taller than the viewport — the overflow must be the body's own box (an absolutely-positioned spacer below body doesn't reliably extend Safari's root scroll range) and must hang off the root scroller, not `<body>`'s own `overflow` (inner scrolling never collapses the bar). Closing/minimizing the player clamps the offset back to 0 without touching `<main>`'s scroll position. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (app-shell CSS block, body class, `lpToggleFullscreen`, fs-button init, `webkitendfullscreen` hook). **Docs:** [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md), [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md).

## [5.26.1] — 2026-06-12
- **Fixed VLC "unable to open the MRL" on Windows files whose full path is 260+ characters (MAX_PATH).** qBittorrent writes such files fine (it uses `\\?\` extended-length paths internally), but VLC opens inputs with the plain Win32 API, so a long multi-episode filename (e.g. a four-part series finale) produced a file that existed on disk yet could never be played — every other episode in the same folder worked. All VLC input URIs are now built through a single helper, `vlc_file_uri()` ([main.py](main.py)), which behaves exactly like the old `Path.resolve().as_uri()` except on Windows paths over 259 chars, where it substitutes the 8.3 short form (`GetShortPathNameW`) that stays under the limit. Round-tripping is safe — everything that maps VLC's reported URI back to a library path goes through `Path.resolve()`, which expands short names back to the canonical long path. Falls back to the long URI (with a log warning) if 8.3 name generation is disabled on the volume. **Docs:** [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md), [docs/BACKEND.md](docs/BACKEND.md).

## [5.26.0] — 2026-06-11
- **On-device player: the video now takes the entire screen, and the track/clip controls moved behind a gear button — fixing the mobile layout overflow.** The 5.25.0 player kept the header and the always-visible track row (quality/audio/sub/AI/clip — up to ~200px tall) as flex siblings of the video, which both shrank the video and overflowed short mobile viewports. Now **everything overlays the video**: `#lpStage` is `absolute inset:0` (the video gets every pixel, nothing can overflow), the header (`#lpHeader`) is an absolute translucent top bar, and the old track row (`#lpTrackRow`) became an **options panel** — hidden until the new **gear button** in the bottom control strip toggles it (`lpToggleOpts`, `.lp-opts` on `#localPlayer`), anchored above the transport, scrollable, max 380px wide. While the panel is open the overlay never auto-hides; a tap on the video closes the panel first. On narrow phones (≤480px) the header buttons collapse to icons (`.lp-btn-label`) so the bar can't overflow either. The bottom strip now carries the safe-area inset itself (the old `safe-bottom` spacer div is gone). **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`#lpStage`/`#lpHeader`/`#lpTrackRow` CSS, `#lpOptsBtn`, `lpToggleOpts`/`_lpOptsOpen`, guards in `_lpCtlShow`/`_lpCtlIdle`/`lpStageTap`, cleanup in `lpStop`/`lpMinimize`). **Docs:** [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md), [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.25.0] — 2026-06-11
- **The on-device player now draws its own Metro-style controls instead of the browser's native `<video>` chrome — so the player looks and behaves identically on every OS and browser.** Native controls vary wildly across platforms (different seek bars, different/missing subtitle menus, iOS hijacking fullscreen into its own player), so users saw a different UI depending on their device. The `controls` attribute is gone; a custom overlay (`#lpControls`) provides: a **seek bar** with buffered indicator and drag-to-scrub (position previews while dragging, a single seek commits on release — important in on-demand mode where every cold seek restarts the JIT encode), **±10 s tiles**, a center **play/pause tile**, **current/total time**, **mute**, and **fullscreen** — which fullscreens the whole player container (header, transport, audio/sub/quality selectors all stay visible and usable inside OS fullscreen) rather than the bare video, keeping the custom UI on-screen. Mobile-first: 44 px+ touch targets, tap the video to toggle the overlay (auto-hides after 3 s while playing; never while paused, scrubbing, buffering, or reconnecting), square Metro buffering spinner shown on any data stall, all chrome fades opacity-only (no reflow). Desktop additions: mouse-move reveals controls, keyboard shortcuts (Space/K play-pause, ←/→ ±10 s, F fullscreen, M mute). On iPhone Safari (no element-fullscreen API) the fullscreen button hides itself — the player is already a full-viewport overlay. In tiny corner-tile mode the overlay hides and a tap maximizes. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`#lpStage`/`#lpControls`/`#lpBuffSpin` markup + CSS, `lpStageTap`/`_lpCtlShow`/`_lpCtlIdle`/`_lpCtlSync`/`_lpCtlTick`/`lpTogglePlay`/`lpSeekBy`/`lpToggleMute`/`lpToggleFullscreen`/`_lpSeekBarInit`, keyboard handler, `.lp-idle`/`.lp-buffering`/`.lp-scrub` states). **Docs:** [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md), [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.24.0] — 2026-06-11
- **On-device streaming now survives unstable connections (tunnels, Wi-Fi↔LTE swaps) the way YouTube does.** Two root causes fixed: **(1)** the forward buffer was capped at 60 s — and effectively less, since hls.js's default 60 MB `maxBufferSize` byte cap holds only ~60 s of a high-bitrate original rung — so any outage longer than the buffer cut playback out; the player now buffers ~3 minutes ahead (`maxBufferLength: 180`, `maxBufferSize: 240 MB`, with `backBufferLength: 90` freeing memory behind the playhead so mobile devices can afford it). **(2)** a fatal hls.js `NETWORK_ERROR` showed an error alert and stopped loading **forever** — even though the `<video>` element would happily keep playing its buffer and the connection usually comes right back; now playback keeps draining the buffer while a background reconnect loop retries `hls.startLoad()` with backoff (2 s → 15 s cap, indefinitely), recovery detected on `FRAG_LOADED`, with the browser `online` event short-circuiting the backoff (retries deliberately don't gate on `navigator.onLine` — a phone in a tunnel often reports online with no usable data). The Safari-native path gets the same policy: instead of an alert, a video `error` reloads the still-set `src` and seeks back to where playback died (only the permanent `MEDIA_ERR_SRC_NOT_SUPPORTED` still alerts). A "Reconnecting…" overlay appears only once the buffer actually runs dry — outages the buffer covers are invisible. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`_lpNetLost`/`_lpNetRetryNow`/`_lpNetReset`/`_lpNetOnline`, `lp.netDown`, hls.js buffer config, `waiting`/`playing`/`error` listeners). **Docs:** [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md) (§ Unstable connections).

## [5.23.0] — 2026-06-11
- **Smart Skip fingerprinting is dramatically faster, matches intros it used to truncate or miss, and its admin progress bar no longer "restarts".** Three root causes fixed: **(1) Matcher speed + accuracy** — the episode-pair matcher was an O(N²) pure-Python loop (~10-60 s *per pair*) that also demanded a strictly consecutive run of matching frames; since each chromaprint frame spans ~2.4 s of audio, one second of episode-specific audio inside the theme (a title-card voiceover) corrupts ~20 consecutive frames, so real intros got truncated at the first blip or missed entirely. The matcher is now numpy-vectorized (XOR + popcount LUT, ~50-100× faster; pure-Python fallback if numpy is absent) and **bridges mismatch gaps** up to ~4 s (`MATCH_GAP_FRAMES`, `MATCH_MIN_RATIO`) so full intro spans are detected, while a new **stationary-audio guard** (`MIN_FRAME_DELTA_BITS`, `_informative_mask`) stops silence/drones/tones — whose near-identical chromaprint frames bogus-match for tens of seconds — from producing false intro windows. `ANALYZER_VERSION` bumped to 3 → existing libraries re-analyze with the better algorithm. Episodes are also fingerprinted 2-at-a-time (`FP_CONCURRENCY`). **(2) Restarting passes** — analysis was kicked off per prepped file, and every pass re-fingerprints the whole series, so during a season prep the analyzer genuinely restarted from episode 1 over and over (quadratic work). It now **coalesces**: scheduling defers while any prep job for the series is queued/encoding (`_series_prep_active`), with a 15 s watcher (`_watch_prep_then_analyze`) backstopping prep exits that don't fire the post-prep hook — one full pass after the last file lands. **(3) Progress reporting** — the bar was drawn from per-stage `current/total`, which resets at every stage boundary and whose matching-stage `total` is a growing estimate (backward jumps). The analyzer now emits a **monotonic all-stages `progress` fraction** consumed by the Smart Skip badge and Activity tab. Also fixed: **manual skip entries are no longer overwritten** by a series re-run (the docs always promised this; the persistence loop now enforces it). **Backend:** [analyzer.py](analyzer.py) (`_find_longest_match_np`/`_best_gap_run`/`_find_longest_match_py`, gap/ratio constants, parallel fingerprinting, `progress` emit, version 3), [main.py](main.py) (`_series_prep_active`, `_watch_prep_then_analyze`, defer guard in `_schedule_series_analysis_if_eligible`, manual-entry guard in `_run_series_analysis`, Activity snapshot uses `job.progress`). **UI:** [static/admin.html](static/admin.html) (`_statusBadge` uses `job.progress`). **Deps:** [requirements.txt](requirements.txt) (+numpy). **Docs:** [docs/ANALYZER.md](docs/ANALYZER.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.22.0] — 2026-06-09
- **The host-busy banner and the global "Prepping N files" pill are now both collapsible — each starts as a small chevron tab so they no longer clip/block the navbar and corner.** The "Host is busy/overloaded" banner (full-width sticky strip at `z-70`) and the fixed top-right prep pill overlapped the navbar and each other when active. Both now render **collapsed by default**: the banner shrinks to a small tone-coloured chevron tab pinned top-right (rest of the strip transparent + click-through); the prep pill shrinks to just its pulsing dot + chevron. Clicking the chevron expands the full content (and flips the chevron up); clicking again re-collapses. Banner state (`perfBannerExpanded`) is re-applied across the per-SSE-tick `className` rewrites; pill state (`prepBarExpanded`) survives `_renderGlobalPrep`'s re-renders. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`#perfBannerToggle`/`togglePerfBanner`/`renderPerfBanner`/`.perf-collapsed`; `#globalPrepToggle`/`togglePrepBar`/`.prep-collapsed`).

## [5.21.0] — 2026-06-09
- **Background work now drains itself: idle auto-fingerprint + auto-validate, plus an "Outstanding Work" backlog view on the Activity tab.** The Activity tab only ever showed work running *right now* — so with most shows never fingerprinted and almost none validated, it sat empty, because those tasks were only ever triggered manually / on-add. Two changes fix that: **(1)** a new **`background_maintenance_loop`** runs Smart Skip fingerprinting and source-file validation automatically **while the box is idle** (no playback / recent use) at below-normal priority — one series / one file at a time, pausing the instant the box is used. Validation verdicts are **persisted per file** (`library.json → files[].validation`), so the validator skips already-checked files and **resumes after a restart/auto-update instead of starting over** (directly addressing the "restarts interrupt progress that doesn't restart" problem). **(2)** the Activity tab gained an **Outstanding Work** card showing the backlog counts (un-prepped / un-fingerprinted / never-validated) and *why each isn't running* (e.g. "Auto-fingerprint is ON — runs while idle" vs "Auto-validate is OFF"). New admin **Automatic Maintenance** card (System tab) toggles the two workers (default ON). **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`background_maintenance_loop`, `_run_auto_validation`, `_auto_maint_cfg`, persisted-verdict helpers `_file_sig`/`_needs_validation`/`_persist_validations`, backlog helpers, `GET`/`POST /api/admin/auto-maintenance`, `AppState.auto_validate*`, manual scans now persist verdicts too, `_activity_snapshot.outstanding`). **UI:** [static/admin.html](static/admin.html) (Outstanding Work card, Automatic Maintenance toggles). **Docs:** [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/BACKEND.md](docs/BACKEND.md), [docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md](docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md).

## [5.20.0] — 2026-06-09
- **New admin "Activity" tab shows every background job, *why* it's running, and whether it survives a restart.** Server restarts and auto-updates were silently discarding in-flight work (HLS stream prep, AI subtitles, file validation/repair, Smart Skip analysis, on-demand transcode sessions) — none of it checkpoints, so a progress bar that "reset" was actually a fresh start under a restarted process, with no indication why. The new tab (now the admin landing tab) lists each active job with a plain-English reason and a **Lost on restart** vs **Survives restart** badge, plus a summary strip (active count, fragile count, host idle/busy, Auto-Prep mode, prep-paused / force-prep-stopped / VPN-down gates) and a heads-up banner when restarting now would interrupt non-resumable work. Auto-refreshes every 4 s while open. Torrent downloads are flagged as surviving (qBittorrent persists them out-of-process); everything in-memory is flagged fragile, with notes on what re-queues automatically (bulk auto-prep) vs. what must be re-triggered (Force Prep, file validation/repair). **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`_activity_title`, `_activity_snapshot`, `GET /api/admin/activity`). **UI:** [static/admin.html](static/admin.html) (Activity tab + `loadActivity`/`startActivityPolling`). **Docs:** [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md).

## [5.19.0] — 2026-06-09
- **Admin can now choose which network adapter is the server's primary address — every other adapter still answers but redirects to the chosen one.** A new **Network Adapter** card (System tab) lists the host's physical LAN adapters; picking one stores its interface *name* (so it survives DHCP IP changes) and makes that adapter's current IP the single canonical address. uvicorn stays bound to `0.0.0.0`, so the dashboard keeps answering on every adapter — but a client that connects on a non-preferred adapter's IP is 307-redirected to the primary (e.g. Wi-Fi `192.168.0.104` → Ethernet `192.168.0.106`). The preferred adapter is also what `remote.local` (mDNS) and the printed URL resolve to. **Preference + graceful fallback:** if the chosen adapter is offline, the server falls back to the route-table heuristic, advertises that instead, and logs the issue (once, not on every keepalive poll); the admin card surfaces the fallback inline. **New shared module** [netadapters.py](netadapters.py) holds the adapter enumeration + preferred-adapter resolution (the logic lifted out of `run.py`'s `get_local_ip`), imported by both the launcher and the dashboard. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`AppState.preferred_adapter`, `_network_cfg`, `network_adapter_redirect` middleware, `_network_status`, `NetworkReq`, `GET`/`POST /api/admin/network`, lifespan seed). **Launcher:** [run.py](run.py) (`get_local_ip` now delegates to `netadapters` + reads the preferred adapter + logs fallback on change). **UI:** [static/admin.html](static/admin.html) (Network Adapter card + `loadNetwork`/`saveNetwork`). **Docs:** [docs/RUNTIME.md](docs/RUNTIME.md), [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.18.0] — 2026-06-09
- **UI responsiveness pass — every control that waits on the server now shows an immediate pending state (spinner + dim + disable) and clears it when done.** Previously many actions fired a request and gave no feedback until the response landed — the prime example being the Library **Refresh** button, which looked inert whether it had refreshed or was still waiting. This standardises the existing `withInflight`/`_markLoading` spinner across the dashboard and ports the same helper into the admin panel (which had none). **Dashboard ([static/index.html](static/index.html)):** Refresh (`loadLibrary`), search, add/remove storage path, mark-watched, recheck, delete item, queue/cancel play-when-ready, download/profile/change-PIN submits, the per-file & per-season download/idle/skip schedule segments, and the stream-prep schedule buttons all spin while in flight (and drop double-taps). **Admin ([static/admin.html](static/admin.html)):** ported the `withInflight`/`_markLoading` helper + spinner CSS, then wired login, every Save (subtitles, STT, qBit limits, categories, TMDb, env keys, indexer config, scheduled restart, auto-prep, auto-update, skip-data, cache auto-purge), every Refresh/Load (indexers, logs, components, changelog, offline cache, analyzer log), component install, force-prep / file-validate / file-repair start+stop, cache purge/delete, branch/commit switch + hard-reset, shutdown/reboot, and PIN save. Controls that already showed strong feedback (upload progress bars, in-region "Loading…/Searching…" text) were left as-is. **Docs:** [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md).

## [5.17.0] — 2026-06-08
- **Holding the fullscreen "To Device" tile while it's mid-prep now starts on-device playback immediately via the JIT path, instead of doing nothing.** When an un-prepped library file is playing on the TV, holding the tile starts a full prep and the tile flips to "Prepping 42%". Previously a second hold during that state was a no-op — you had to wait out the whole encode before you could move playback to your device. Now holding the "Prepping…" tile hands off to this device **right away** using on-demand (just-in-time) streaming (`_lpLoadIndex`'s existing un-prepped fallback), while the full ABR bundle keeps building in the background for a later, richer play. The tile now advertises this ("Hold to stream here now"). **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`fcDeviceTileHold` prepping branch, `handoffToDevice(btn, allowOnDemand)`, `_renderFcHandoff` prepping note). **Docs:** [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md).

## [5.16.1] — 2026-06-08
- **File repair no longer strips embedded subtitles during the lossy re-encode pass.** The remux repair leg already preserved every stream (`-map 0 -c copy`), but the opt-in **re-encode** fallback mapped only video + audio (`-map 0:v:0? -map 0:a?`), so repairing a genuinely-corrupt file by re-encoding silently dropped all baked-in subtitle tracks. The re-encode now also carries embedded subtitles (`-map 0:s?`) and, in MKV, attachments such as ASS fonts (`-map 0:t?`): subs are copied as-is for MKV (image subs like PGS/VOBSUB included) and transcoded to `mov_text` for MP4/MOV (where copying subrip fails). Sidecar subtitles — including online-downloaded and deep-discovered (`Subs/`-folder) `.srt`s — were already preserved, since repair replaces the source in place (`os.replace`) keeping the same path/stem they're keyed on. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`_repair_one_file` re-encode attempt). **Docs:** [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.16.0] — 2026-06-08
- **Automatic stream prep can now validate & repair each source file as it preps it — GPU-accelerated, admin-controlled, off by default.** A new **Validate & Repair on Prep** card (System tab) adds a three-way mode so the unattended overnight/idle prep run can also heal corrupt media without anyone remembering to run the manual File Validator: **Don't Validate** (default, current behaviour), **Repair Before Prep** (deep-decode the source first and lossless **remux-repair** it in place if damaged, then prep the healed file), and **Repair After Prep** (build the HLS bundle first, then deep-decode the source — a repair purges the just-built bundle so it re-preps from the healed source next cycle). It reuses the existing per-file `_validate_one_file`/`_repair_one_file` (remux-only, no lossy re-encode) and runs **only for bulk & idle preps** — interactive play-on-device preps are never delayed. The validator/repair `ffmpeg` now **decodes on the GPU when NVENC is present** (transparent `-hwaccel cuda`, with a CPU fallback), and the optional repair re-encode uses `h264_nvenc`; this applies to the manual File Validator too. The scan/repair runs inside the prep concurrency slot (one ffmpeg at a time) and its live process is the prep job's, so the existing **Pause / Stop Now / activity-kick** controls terminate it for free. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`PrepValidateReq`, `_prep_validate_cfg`, `GET`/`POST /api/admin/prep-validate`, `_decode_hwaccel_args`, `_prep_validate_repair`, before/after hooks in `_run_offline_job`, `set_proc`/`is_stopped` params on `_validate_one_file`/`_repair_one_file`). **UI:** [static/admin.html](static/admin.html) (Validate & Repair on Prep card + `loadPrepValidate`/`setPrepValidate`/`_renderPrepValidate`). **Docs:** [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md), [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md](docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.15.0] — 2026-06-07
- **New admin File Validator card (System tab) — decode your source files with ffmpeg to find damaged/corrupt media, separate from the torrent recheck.** The qBit recheck only proves the bytes on disk match the torrent's hashes, so it happily seeds a perfect copy of a file that was *already* damaged at the source (bad encode, truncated rip, bit-rot before it was added). The validator actually **decodes the media**: a **Deep** scan (default) runs each library video through `ffmpeg -v error -xerror -i … -map 0:v? -map 0:a? -f null -` and flags any file that produces a decode error (catches mid-file corruption a header probe misses); a **Quick** scan just ffprobes the container (opens / has a video stream / has a duration). Scope is the whole library or one item. ffmpeg runs **below normal priority** and one file at a time so a scan can't starve playback; **Stop** halts the loop between files and terminates the in-flight decode. Damaged + missing-on-disk files are listed with the ffmpeg error tail. Works on every OS (plain decode — not HLS, so unlike prep it is **not** macOS-gated). **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`ValidateFilesReq`, `AppState.file_validation*`, `_validate_one_file`, `_run_file_validation`, `_file_validation_status`, `GET`/`POST /api/admin/validate-files`, `POST /api/admin/validate-files/stop`). **UI:** [static/admin.html](static/admin.html) (File Validator card + `loadFileValidation`/`startFileValidation`/`stopFileValidation` + 2 s poll). **Docs:** [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md).
- **File Validator can now attempt to repair the damaged files it finds.** Once a scan turns up damaged files, a **Repair Damaged** control appears. Each file is fixed in two staged, validated attempts: a lossless **remux** (`-c copy` with `-err_detect ignore_err` + regenerated timestamps — fixes broken index/moov/PTS and recoverable stream errors), then — if you tick **Allow lossy re-encode** — a libx264 **re-encode** that drops/conceals genuinely corrupt frames. The candidate is run back through the same deep decode and the original is **replaced only if it now decodes clean**, after which its stale on-device HLS bundle is purged so playback re-preps from the repaired source. Repaired/failed files are listed; **Stop** halts between files. **Caveat surfaced in the UI:** rewriting a file stops a torrent-backed copy from seeding (its bytes no longer match the pieces) — repair targets uploaded / non-torrent content; re-download is the better fix for torrent files. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`RepairFilesReq`, `AppState.file_repair*`, `_repair_one_file`, `_run_file_repair`, `_file_repair_status`, shared `_run_ffmpeg_capture`/`_ffmpeg_decode_scan`/`_safe_unlink`, `GET`/`POST /api/admin/repair-files`, `POST /api/admin/repair-files/stop`). **UI:** [static/admin.html](static/admin.html) (repair row + `startFileRepair`/`stopFileRepair`/`_renderFileRepair` + 2 s poll). **Docs:** [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md).

## [5.14.0] — 2026-06-07
- **The episode-picker scheduling bar gains a stream-prep schedule (Now / Idle / Never), hides the download buttons once everything's downloaded, and adds a Recheck-hashes button.** The bar in the episode page that controlled *what downloads and when* (`⬇ Now / 🌙 Idle / ⊘ Skip`) was reworked into a three-row control:
  - **Stream-prep schedule (`⚡ Now / 🌙 Idle / ⊘ Never`)** — the HLS-prep sibling of the download schedule, applied to the visible season's files. **Now** preps them immediately (a scoped `/prep-all`), **Idle** lets Automatic Stream Prep build the bundle while the box is idle (the implicit default), **Never** opts the files out of *all* auto-prep — the idle/always `auto_prep_loop` and the play-driven warm-prep chain both skip "never" files, while any already-built bundle is kept (non-destructive). The active mode is highlighted, and a persisted per-file mode lives in `library.json → item["prep"]["files"]`.
  - **Download buttons hidden when fully downloaded** — the `⬇ Now / 🌙 Idle / ⊘ Skip` download row only appears while at least one episode still needs fetching; once every file in the item is on disk, scheduling what to download is moot, so the row is hidden (the prep + recheck rows stay).
  - **Recheck hashes** — a new button runs a qBittorrent piece-level **force-recheck** of the item's torrent over the **checked** episodes, waits for it to finish, and for any file that was complete but comes back damaged it re-fetches the bad pieces and **invalidates that file's cached HLS bundle** so it re-preps from the repaired source.
  **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`_PREP_MODES`/`_prep_cfg`/`_effective_prep_mode`, `prep_mode` in `/files`, `POST /api/library/{id}/prep-schedule`, `POST /api/library/{id}/recheck`, `qbit_recheck`, "never" gate in `_enqueue_library_prep` + `_play_prep_chain`). **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`renderEpList` bar, `_epPrepBtn`, `epSchedPrep`, `epRecheckSelected`, `_visibleSeasonFiles`/`_visibleSeasonPrepMode`). **Docs:** [docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md](docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md), [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md).

## [5.13.0] — 2026-06-07
- **Scrub bar is now locked by default — a guided hold-then-release gesture unlocks it — so accidental taps can't fling playback, and the mobile scrub timestamp no longer gets stuck over the bar.** The seek bar (both the footer bar and the fullscreen-controls bar) defaults to a **LOCKED** state: the track is greyed out (`grayscale` + dimmed) with a centred **HOLD TO UNLOCK** padlock badge, and any tap/click is ignored. Unlocking is a deliberate **three-phase gesture, all phases still locked** so neither the hold nor the release that ends it can be misread as a seek: (1) a **0.5s press-and-hold** (badge "HOLD TO UNLOCK", indigo fill grows; a too-short release aborts); (2) the badge then turns green and **pulses "RELEASE"** and just **waits for the user to lift — no timer runs**, so gripping the whole time can never lead to an accidental seek; (3) **only once they release** does a final **0.5s settle** (green fill re-sweep, "UNLOCKING…") run before the bar becomes seekable. Once unlocked it seeks normally and **re-locks 5s** after the last interaction (and immediately whenever playback stops, so every new stream starts protected). The handlers were rewritten from the old mouse+touch pair (`onclick`/`ontouch*` → `handleSeekBarClick`) to unified **Pointer Events** (`handleSeekPointerDown`/`Up`/`Leave`), which also fixes a mobile bug: on `touchend` the old code read `e.touches[0].clientX` from an empty (but truthy) `TouchList`, throwing a `TypeError` before `handleSeekBarLeave()` could run — so the scrub timestamp tooltip never hid and hovered over the bar. Pointer events always carry `clientX`, and the tooltip also gained a 2s safety auto-hide. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`.seekBar`/`.seekLockBadge`/`.seekUnlockProgress` + `holding`/`ready`/`settling` CSS, both seek-bar markup blocks, `handleSeekPointerDown`/`Up`/`Leave`, `_doSeek`/`lockSeekBar`/`unlockSeekBar`/`_cancelArming`, `updateState` re-lock). **Docs:** [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md).

## [5.12.0] — 2026-06-07
- **Dashboard now uses the full width of the screen with responsive multi-column grids (Metro polish).** The whole app shell (navbar, main content, player footer) was pinned to a centered `max-w-5xl` (1024px) column, leaving large dead margins on wide desktops/TVs — our Windows-primary target. Raised the shell cap to `max-w-screen-2xl` (1536px) and converted the three list surfaces to responsive grids that add columns as the viewport grows, while staying single-column (mobile-first) on phones: **Search results** → 1 / 2 / 3 columns (`sm` / `xl`), **Library cards** → 1 / 2 columns (`lg`), **Episode list** → 1 / 2 columns (`xl`). Search-result Save/Play buttons were also brought back to the Metro convention (bold uppercase). No behaviour change — purely layout/space-usage and styling. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`#resultsGrid` + `doSearch` card buttons, `renderLibrary` group wrappers, `renderEpList` unwatched/watched wrappers, shell `max-w` cap). **Docs:** [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md).
- **Library cards: single-item series now span full width (no stranded empty column), and the card button row is clean on mobile.** A series with only one item was leaving the second grid column empty, so the list looked ragged — `renderLibrary` now only goes 2-up when a series actually has multiple items (`gridCls`). The per-card action row was reworked: primary buttons (`.lib-card-actions > button`) are forced to a uniform 44px height on a single line — no more 2-line "☰ / Episodes" wrap or mismatched button heights — and the icon-only buttons (download / prep / hide / delete) collect into one cluster (`iconBtns`) that follows immediately (the earlier `ml-auto` was absorbing the row's slack and leaving a sparse gap). The symbol glyphs in the primary buttons (`↩` Resume, `▶` Play/Restart/When-Ready, `⏸` Idle, `⏳` Queued) carry a `︎` text-presentation selector so iOS renders them as flat monochrome Metro glyphs instead of rounded colour emoji. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`renderLibrary`, `.lib-card-actions` CSS).
- **Mobile landscape is usable again — episode picker, player footer, and fullscreen controls.** Phones in landscape are only ~320-430px tall, and the portrait-sized chrome ate the whole screen. Three breakages, all fixed by a new `@media (orientation:landscape) and (max-height:500px)` block (tablets ≈744px+ tall are unaffected): (1) the **episode page** hero (poster + overview + chips + season tabs + action bar) left **zero** height for the episode list — it now becomes a **two-pane split**: the hero (series art + description) is a scrollable left column at ~¼ width and the season tabs + episode list + actions (wrapped in a new `#epRightPane`) fill the right ¾; (2) the **player footer** row heights are trimmed so the library stays browsable; (3) the **fullscreen player controls** stacked up to six `flex-1` tile rows that got crushed below their content and overlapped into an unreadable pile — the tile grid (`#fcTileGrid`) now gives each row its natural min-height and scrolls instead. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (landscape `<style>` block, `#epRightPane`/`#epHeroContent`/`#fcTileGrid` hooks).

## [5.11.2] — 2026-06-07
- **Fix: server notice banners no longer block the on-device player's Stop / To TV buttons on mobile.** The server-attention and host-performance banners float at `z-70` — above the on-device player (`z-50`) and its top control bar — so whenever one showed (most commonly the host-busy perf banner during stream prep), it sat over the **Stop** and **To TV** buttons and swallowed every tap aimed at them on mobile. The banners are purely informational, so they're now `pointer-events:none` (set by ID so it survives the className rewrites in `renderServerAttention`/`renderPerfBanner`); only the Admin Panel link re-enables clicks. The banners and the error/warning toast were also made translucent (`/95`→`/70`, toast `/80`→`/70`) so they sit lightly over the video instead of fully obscuring it. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (banner `pointer-events` CSS, `ALERT_STYLES`, `renderServerAttention`/`renderPerfBanner` tones).

## [5.11.1] — 2026-06-07
- **Fix: Smart Skip fingerprinting no longer freezes the dashboard.** While a fingerprint pass reached its matching stage, the UI would go unresponsive for a minute or two — inputs taking ages to register — even though the host itself (RDP, CPU, RAM) looked perfectly healthy. Cause: the intro/credits matcher (`analyzer._find_longest_match`) is ~10-20 s of tight **pure-Python** CPU work per episode pair, and although it was already offloaded with `asyncio.to_thread`, a *thread* doesn't release the GIL for pure-Python work — the GIL convoy effect starved the server's event loop. The matcher now runs in a separate one-worker **process** (`ProcessPoolExecutor`, dropped to BELOW_NORMAL priority) so the work is on a fully independent GIL and the dashboard stays snappy; it falls back to the old thread path if a host can't create a process pool. Same results, same speed — just off the event loop. (In a local A/B the worst event-loop stall dropped from ~25 ms to ~9 ms on an *idle* box; the win is far larger under real server load.) **Analyzer:** [analyzer.py](analyzer.py) (`_new_match_executor`, `_match_worker_init`, `_run_match`, `_build_clusters_async`/`analyze_series` wiring). **Docs:** [docs/ANALYZER.md](docs/ANALYZER.md) (§ Concurrency), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md) (`to_thread` doesn't help pure-Python CPU).

## [5.11.0] — 2026-06-07
- **Smart Skip audio fingerprinting now runs as part of stream prep instead of the moment a download finishes — and a failed file no longer keeps retrying forever.** Previously intro/credits fingerprinting fired on every completed download (`library_download_monitor`'s ready-flip), and a file that failed to fingerprint re-ran on *every* sibling that later became ready — churning the analyzer pointlessly. Now fingerprinting is triggered once a file's HLS bundle is built (`_ensure_analysis_for` at the end of `_run_offline_job`, the post-prep sibling of the AI-subtitle hook), so it only runs on content you actually prep. The trigger is **fire-and-forget** — it just schedules a per-series pass at lowered OS priority and never blocks or fails the prep — and a running-guard stops a bulk `Prep for Streaming` of a big series from stacking duplicate passes. **Failures are now sticky:** a file that fails fingerprinting is not auto-retried; it re-runs only when the analyzer version is bumped or when an admin clicks **Analyze** in the Smart Skip tab. (Trade-off: content that is never stream-prepped no longer gets intro/credits skip data; auto-prep being on by default covers the normal case. On macOS, where stream prep is disabled by the TCC block, fingerprinting no longer runs at all — the analyzer's ffmpeg/fpcalc children were already blocked there anyway.) **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`_ensure_analysis_for`, post-prep hook in `_run_offline_job`, running-guard + no-auto-retry in `_schedule_series_analysis_if_eligible` / `_needs_reanalysis`, removed the `library_download_monitor` trigger). **Docs:** [docs/ANALYZER.md](docs/ANALYZER.md), [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.10.0] — 2026-06-07
- **Admins can now choose how far the VPN kill switch reaches.** A new **VPN Kill Switch** card on the admin System tab toggles between two modes: **Block UI** (the existing behaviour — a Mullvad drop locks the whole dashboard behind the full-screen "VPN DISCONNECTED" overlay) and **qBit Only** (only qBittorrent is killed and the torrent stream/download endpoints stay blocked, but the rest of the UI keeps working so a viewer can still watch already-prepped on-device content). **Regardless of the choice, qBittorrent is always killed the instant the VPN drops** — that invariant is enforced unconditionally by `vpn_guard` (in-process) and `watchdog.py` (process level); the new setting governs only the UI lockout. Persists under `library.json → settings.vpn_killswitch.block_ui` (default `true`), mirrored into `state.vpn_block_ui` and broadcast in the `state` / `vpn_status` SSE events so the overlay appears/clears live. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`_vpn_killswitch_cfg`, `AppState.vpn_block_ui`, `GET`/`POST /api/admin/vpn-killswitch`, `vpn_guard` broadcast, `state_snapshot`). **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`renderVpn` block-UI gate), [static/admin.html](static/admin.html) (VPN Kill Switch card, `loadVpnKillswitch`/`toggleVpnKillswitch`). **Docs:** [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md](docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md), [docs/DAEMON_WATCHDOG.md](docs/DAEMON_WATCHDOG.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.9.0] — 2026-06-07
- **Admins in developer mode can now pin the dashboard to an exact commit.** The Updates tab's developer-mode area gains a **Pin To Commit** field (shown only when *Show all branches* is ticked): enter a 7–40 hex SHA (e.g. `f8e920a40fd8`) and click **Pin Commit** to hard-checkout that exact build as a **detached HEAD** — useful for reproducing a regression on a specific commit. While pinned, **the auto-updater is disabled** (there's no branch to track, so it would silently yank you off the pinned build); a banner on the tab explains this and the status loop stands down. To re-enable auto-update, pick a branch and click **Switch Branch** (or **Apply Now**) to return to a branch. The commit-pin is developer-only and gated server-side — the SHA is structurally validated (hex, 7–40 chars) so it can't smuggle in a refspec or git option injection. **Backend:** [updater.py](updater.py) (`switch_commit`, `is_detached_head`, `_looks_like_commit`), [main.py](main.py) (`POST /api/admin/updater/switch-commit`, `detached_head` in `GET /api/admin/updater`, detached-HEAD guard in `updater_loop`). **UI:** [static/admin.html](static/admin.html) (`switchCommitNow`, `_renderCommitPin`, detached-HEAD notice). **Docs:** [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md).

## [5.8.0] — 2026-06-07
- **Server notices (errors, warnings, server reboot, network/host warnings) now stay visible on every screen — including the fullscreen player controls — without blocking the UI.** Previously the top banners (reboot/update, host-busy) and the error/warning toast were hidden behind the opaque fullscreen-controls overlay and could be covered by modals. Now: (1) the banners + toast sit above modals so a notice is never lost behind a dialog; and (2) while the fullscreen VLC controls are open, those top elements are swapped for a **dedicated notice strip** (`#fcNotice`) overlaid on the title row. The strip is **absolutely positioned so it never reflows the control tiles below** — users rely on muscle memory for Play/Seek/Volume, so the buttons must not shift — and it's `pointer-events:none` so it can never block a control. The strip mirrors whatever the live banners/toast are saying (reboot/update first, then host performance/network, then the latest alert), tone-coloured to match. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`renderFcNotice`, `_fcNoticeTone`, `body.fc-open` handling in `openFullscreenControls`/`closeFullscreenControls`, raised z-index on `#globalToast`/`#serverAttentionBanner`/`#perfBanner`). **Docs:** [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md).

## [5.7.0] — 2026-06-07
- **The admin Updates tab now shows the changelog and warns about risky branches.** Three additions to the auto-updater panel: (1) a **Changelog** card renders `CHANGELOG.md` (newest first, lightly formatted) so an admin can see exactly what each release changed before — or after — applying an update; (2) selecting **alpha** now surfaces a severe inline warning that the branch may break StreamLink and require a manual reinstall, while **beta** shows a milder "issues may be present" note; and (3) ticking **Show all branches (developer mode)** now warns that not all branches are functional and switching to one may cause data loss and require a full reinstall. Warnings update live as the branch picker / dev-mode toggle change. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`GET /api/admin/updater/changelog`). **UI:** [static/admin.html](static/admin.html) (`loadChangelog`, `_renderChangelogMd`, `_renderBranchWarning`). **Docs:** [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md).

## [5.6.0] — 2026-06-07
- **Skipping to the next episode now marks the one you left as watched no matter where you skipped from.** Previously the deferred "mark watched" only armed when you jumped within the **last quarter** of the episode; skip earlier and it never tripped. Now any skip to the next episode — via the **Next** button, the **Skip Credits → Next** offer, or auto-skip-credits — arms the watched timer. The **~60 s grace period is unchanged**: if you skipped by mistake (or were dodging real content), just return to that episode within the window and your real progress is left untouched (the timer cancels the moment you're back on that file). One timer at a time — a newer skip supersedes an older pending one. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`_arm_credit_skip_watch` — dropped the `CREDIT_SKIP_WATCH_MIN_PCT` last-quarter gate). **Docs:** [docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md](docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md), [docs/ANALYZER.md](docs/ANALYZER.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md).

## [5.5.1] — 2026-06-07
- **The nightly scheduled reboot no longer interrupts in-progress stream prep.** The reboot's idle guard already treated an active download as "in use" (so a download would defer the reboot), but **idle stream-prep / AI-subtitle (STT) jobs were not checked** — and those run precisely when the box is otherwise idle, which is exactly when the reboot wants to fire. Because HLS prep can't checkpoint, a reboot mid-encode threw the work away and it restarted from scratch on the next idle stretch. The reboot now also defers while any HLS-prep or STT job is actively encoding (any queue) or a user/admin-priority prep is queued, re-checking after `idle_minutes` just like the "machine in use" case. Soft-paused files still finishing their current encode are caught; jobs parked at the pause gate (`paused`) correctly don't hold off the reboot. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`_prep_in_progress`, `scheduled_reboot_loop`). **Docs:** [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/BACKEND.md](docs/BACKEND.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.5.0] — 2026-06-07
- **Auto-updates now archive the old version's logs and start the new one with a clean slate.** Previously `streamlink_app.log` / `hls.log` just kept growing across updates, mixing lines from many versions into one file. When an update is applied, the updater drops a marker so that — on the post-update restart, **before any log handler opens a file** (avoiding the Windows "can't touch an open log" trap) — every current log file in `logs/` is zipped into **`logs_old_<timestamp>.zip`** and the originals are cleared. The zip is best-effort per file: an open file is still safely captured (read is always allowed), and a file another live process holds open (e.g. `streamlink_service.log` on Windows) is left in place rather than failing the rotation. **Logs now also carry their version going forward:** every process start logs a `StreamLink v<x.y.z> starting — branch=… commit=…` banner, so a fresh (or freshly-rotated) log clearly identifies which build produced the lines beneath it. (Also brings the stale `UI_VERSION` constant back in sync with the badge.) **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`_archive_old_logs`, `_ROTATE_MARKER`, `_init_logging`, `_log_version_banner`, marker write in `_run_apply`). **Docs:** [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md), [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md).

## [5.4.1] — 2026-06-07
- **Fix: the admin "Download All (.zip)" log bundle now extracts on Windows, and the service log downloads reliably.** The bundle was streamed through an OS pipe, which is non-seekable — that forced `zipfile` to emit **data descriptors** (general-purpose bit 3) with zero CRC/sizes in every local file header. macOS and 7-Zip read the central directory so they coped, but **Windows Explorer's built-in extractor reads the local headers and rejected the archive as "invalid"** (our primary target couldn't open its own log bundle). The bundle is now built into a *seekable* temp file so `zipfile` back-patches real local headers, and each member is read through its own handle so a log another process is actively appending to (notably `streamlink_service.log`, held open by the service-wrapper process) is still captured. Separately, the per-file download now serves a stable **snapshot copy** of the requested log instead of streaming the live file, which is why `streamlink_service.log` — the one log written by a different process and growing continuously — previously failed to download; if the copy can't be read it now returns a clear 500 instead of silently failing. Both responses clean up their temp file via a background task. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`admin_download_logs_bundle`, `admin_download_log`). **Docs:** [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.4.0] — 2026-06-07
- **The dashboard now recovers its live connection reliably after a phone locks or you switch apps.** Previously the realtime (SSE) link could die while the device was suspended and never come back — the UI sat frozen showing stale download/playback state until a manual refresh. Two failure modes are now handled: (1) when the browser fully *closes* the event stream (it gives up after backgrounding), the client rebuilds it itself with exponential backoff instead of waiting on the browser's auto-reconnect (which doesn't fire for a closed stream); and (2) a *half-open* connection (the socket silently died while suspended but still reports OPEN, so no error ever fires) is now caught by a liveness watchdog — the server emits a `ping` event at least every 20 s, and if the client hears nothing for ~50 s it tears the socket down and reconnects. The connection is also re-checked the instant the page returns to the foreground (`visibilitychange` / `pageshow` / `focus`) and when the network comes back (`online`), which is the high-value path on mobile. Reconnects always close the prior stream first so stale/duplicate server-side queues don't pile up. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`/api/events` heartbeat is now a named `ping` event instead of a bare comment line). **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html) (`connectSSE` reconnect supervision, `_ensureSSEConnected`, liveness watchdog, foreground/online re-check). **Docs:** [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.3.1] — 2026-06-07
- **Fix: the fullscreen ±10s / ±30s seek icons drew their inner triangle outside the circle.** The forward (+10/+30) tiles rendered the play-arrow well *above* the surrounding circle, and the rewind (−10/−30) arrow sat inside the circle but noticeably offset to the left — both had been wrong since the icons were added. The inner triangle subpaths are now centered on the circle's center (12,12) and are proper mirror images of each other. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html).

## [5.3.0] — 2026-06-07
- **Skipping to the next episode near the end now marks the one you left as watched.** When you jump to the next episode from within the **last quarter** of the current one — whether via the **Next** button, the **Skip Credits → Next** offer, or auto-skip-credits — you've almost certainly finished it and were just dodging the credits/ending, but the normal "watched" threshold (92%) wouldn't have tripped yet. StreamLink now arms a short **grace timer** (~60 s): if you don't come back to that episode, it's marked watched. If Smart Skip guessed the credits **early** and you were actually skipping real content, just return to the episode within the window and your real progress is left untouched (the timer cancels the moment you're back on that file). One timer at a time — a newer skip supersedes an older pending one. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`_arm_credit_skip_watch` / `_credit_skip_watch_grace` / `_mark_file_watched_internal`, `state.pending_watch`, armed in `/api/vlc/next`, `/api/skip-now` (credits), and the auto-skip-credits countdown; cancelled on return in `vlc_progress_tracker`). **Docs:** [docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md](docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md), [docs/ANALYZER.md](docs/ANALYZER.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md).

## [5.2.0] — 2026-06-06
- **Consolidated automatic stream-prep into one clear control.** The admin System tab's separate **Overnight Stream Prep** (fixed nightly window) and **Idle Auto-Prep** cards are replaced by a single **Automatic Stream Prep** card with three plain-language modes: **Always** (prep whenever there's anything to prep, regardless of activity), **When Idle** (prep only after the box has been idle, then stop on activity — your choice of a **hard** stop that discards the in-flight file or a **soft** stop that lets it finish), and **Never** (manual only — only playing on the TV and the Force button prep). The fixed nightly time-window is gone; the modes are purely activity-based. **Auto-Prep on Play** and **Force Stream Prep** are unchanged. Existing schedules migrate automatically (any old overnight/idle setting → *When Idle*). **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`settings.auto_prep` + `_auto_prep_cfg`, rewritten `auto_prep_loop`, `GET/POST /api/admin/auto-prep` replacing the four overnight/idle endpoints). **UI:** [static/admin.html](static/admin.html), [static/index.html](static/index.html). **Docs:** [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md), [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md](docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md), [docs/BACKEND.md](docs/BACKEND.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [5.1.1] — 2026-06-06
- **Fix: the admin Offline Cache tab no longer re-walks the whole cache on every open.** On a large ABR cache the recursive size walk took long enough that opening the tab felt broken. The server now caches the inventory snapshot and serves it instantly; the tab shows an **"As of …"** stamp so you know how fresh the numbers are, and the **Refresh** button forces a fresh on-disk re-check (it disables + shows *Checking…* while it works). Deletes and the auto-purge loop invalidate the snapshot so purged bundles never linger in the view. Concurrent opens (or an open racing auto-purge) share one walk via a lock. **Backend:** [main.py](main.py) (`_build_offline_cache_inventory` now snapshots; `?refresh=1` on `GET /api/admin/offline-cache`). **UI:** [static/admin.html](static/admin.html). **Docs:** [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md).

## [5.1.0] — 2026-06-06
- **Clip buttons are now hold-to-activate.** The *Clip Last 30s* and *Clip last…* buttons — on both the fullscreen VLC controls and the on-device player — now require a press-and-hold (same gesture as Stop/Hand-off), with the familiar left-to-right fill showing hold progress. A stray tap no longer kicks off a clip. **UI:** [static/index.html](static/index.html).

## [5.0.1] — 2026-06-06
- **Fix: VLC auto-picked AI subtitles over a real one, and ignored your saved/preferred pick.** When a file had a genuine embedded subtitle whose language VLC couldn't read from a tag (e.g. one titled *"Text with various tags"*) plus an AI-generated sidecar, the AI sub was chosen on every play — and re-selecting your sub on the next episode or on restart didn't stick. Root cause: VLC's *own* sidecar autodetection loaded the AI `.srt` (parsing `eng` from its filename) **before** `_load_all_local_subs` ran, so that pre-loaded track arrived **untagged as AI** and read as a "real English" track. The selection policy then ranked it above the untagged genuine sub (and the misclassification also defeated the lone-real-sub fallback that would otherwise carry your choice across episodes). VLC's sidecar autodetect is now disabled (`--no-sub-autodetect-file`) at all three launch sites so StreamLink is the only thing that loads sidecars — and tags AI subs correctly. Resumed files now load their sidecars up front too, so the subtitle menu stays complete and a saved sidecar pick still resolves. **Docs:** [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md), [docs/STT.md](docs/STT.md).

## [5.0.0] — 2026-06-03
- **New: on-demand (just-in-time) streaming — play a non-prepped file on your device *instantly*.** Previously, playing an episode that hadn't been stream-prepped meant waiting for the **entire** file to encode first ("Building stream… 42%") — minutes on a long episode. Now playback starts almost immediately: the server hands the player a *virtual* HLS playlist (computed from the file's duration, no encoding) and transcodes each 6-second segment **just-in-time** as the player requests it — the Jellyfin/Plex model.
  - **Seek anywhere.** Jump to an un-generated spot and the browser shows a brief **Loading…** state while the server generates exactly that part, then resumes there. Seeking back into an already-generated region is instant.
  - **Switchable audio.** On-demand serves one audio track at a time; switching picks a new track and re-buffers briefly. The full ABR quality menu and seamless multi-audio remain benefits of the fully-prepped bundle.
  - **Best of both:** the first play is on-demand *and* the server kicks off the normal full bundle prep in the background (low-priority), so the **next** play of that file uses the rich multi-audio/ABR bundle automatically.
  - Technical: mpegts segments (self-contained, no fmp4 init-segment mismatch across seeks), video always transcodes with forced keyframes every 6 s so segment *N* maps exactly to `[N*6,(N+1)*6)`, per-(source+audio) transcode sessions reaped after 90 s idle. New `POST /api/library/{id}/stream-ondemand`, `GET /api/library/ondemand/{key}/{master.m3u8|media.m3u8|seg_N.ts}`, `POST /api/library/ondemand/{key}/close`. 503 on macOS hosts (no HLS). **Docs:** [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md) § On-Demand, [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md), [docs/BACKEND.md](docs/BACKEND.md).

## [4.27.0] — 2026-06-03
- **New: subtitles get smarter about late-downloaded files, lone options, and your past picks.** Three related changes to how a subtitle track is chosen and remembered:
  - **Upgrade to a real sub when it arrives.** Release `.srt` subtitles routinely finish downloading *after* the video (sequential/streaming download), and discovery happens in waves — so by the time you press play the only usable sub is often the AI-generated one, which then gets applied. The system now keeps watching after playback starts: once a real **preferred-language** sub turns up, it switches to it automatically and shows a brief toast (*"Switched to downloaded English subtitles"*). Runs on **both** players — the TV/VLC path via a server-side watcher (`subtitle_upgrade_loop`), and the on-device player via a 15 s poller (`GET /api/library/{id}/subs`). A manual subtitle pick is never overridden. Admin-toggleable (**on** by default).
  - **A lone subtitle is assumed correct.** When exactly one real subtitle is found and its language can't be read from the filename, it's now treated as the preferred language instead of being skipped in favour of AI. Admin-toggleable (**on** by default).
  - **Per-series subtitle memory.** When you pick a subtitle, that choice (language + whether it was a real, AI, or *off* track) is remembered **per profile, per series** — and re-applied on the next episode, even weeks later. Matching prefers the same kind and falls back across kinds when the exact one isn't present yet (so a remembered "real English" applies the AI track for now and auto-upgrades when the real one lands).
  - **Fix:** the on-device player **never persisted sidecar/AI subtitle picks at all** — `_lpSaveLocalTracks` saved every non-bundle selection as `-1` (off), so a chosen `.srt`/AI sub was forgotten the moment you left the episode. Picks are now saved as a resolvable descriptor (`subtitle_sel`) that survives replays *and* drives the per-series memory above.
  - New `settings.subtitles.upgrade_late_subs` + `single_option` (both default on, in Admin → System → Subtitles); profile `series_subtitle_prefs`; `state` exposes both flags. **Docs:** [docs/STT.md](docs/STT.md), [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md), [docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md](docs/LIBRARY_DATA.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/ADMIN.md](docs/ADMIN.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [4.26.1] — 2026-06-03
- **Fix: server going "incredibly laggy" after a download (with CPU/RAM and the machine itself perfectly fine).** `get_library()` / `put_library()` ran their disk read + `json.loads` + per-item migration (and the `json.dumps`/write) **synchronously on the asyncio event loop**. Hot loops call these constantly during/after a download — `vlc_progress_tracker` every 2 s, `library_download_monitor` every 5 s, plus every API request — and `library.json` grows after each download (the analyzer writes per-file audio-fingerprint `skip_data`). So every few seconds the whole event loop stalled re-parsing/serializing the entire library, which is invisible to CPU% and to the OS (RDP stayed responsive). The collateral was a flood of `httpx.ReadError`s from `https_proxy.py`: the HTTPS proxy's upstream read timed out while the app's loop was blocked. Fix: both helpers now run the blocking I/O via `asyncio.to_thread` while still holding `_lib_lock`, so the loop stays free.
- **Hardening: swept the rest of the codebase for synchronous filesystem work running directly on the event loop** so a big media/cache directory can't reproduce the same loop-stall lag. Now off-loaded to threads: local-subtitle discovery during playback (`_discover_local_subs` in `_load_all_local_subs` — a recursive `rglob` over `Subs/` folders, run on every play), cache-purge artifact deletion (`_delete_cache_artifacts` — recursive size walk + `shutil.rmtree`) in `cache_autopurge_loop` and the three admin offline-cache delete endpoints, the per-poll bundle-size + sidecar-sub walks in the offline/STT job-status endpoints and `offline-prepare`, and `shutil.disk_usage` in `/api/disk-space`. All are plain `await asyncio.to_thread(...)` wraps of existing pure-FS helpers — no behaviour change.
- **Also:** brought the stale `UI_VERSION` constant (was `4.13.0`) back in sync with the page badge so the client-side auto-reload version check works again.

## [4.26.0] — 2026-06-03
- **New: "Clip" — save & share the last 30 seconds (or a custom length) of whatever's playing.** A new clip control appears in two places: the **fullscreen VLC controls** (clips what's on the TV) and the **on-device player**, where it sits directly under the subtitle selector. Each spot leads with a prominent **Clip Last 30s** button and offers a quieter **Clip last…** button for a custom length (1–300 s).
  - The server cuts a standalone, universally-compatible **MP4 (H.264 + AAC, +faststart)** from the original source ending at the live playback position — re-encoded so it plays/AirDrops anywhere. NVENC when available, else libx264. On mobile the finished clip is handed to the OS **share sheet** (`navigator.share`); on desktop it downloads.
  - **Prepped-only:** clipping requires the file to already be stream-prepped (the HLS bundle on disk). The fullscreen tiles grey out until the episode is prepped; on-device the file is prepped by definition. Backend returns 409 with a hint otherwise.
  - Clips are ephemeral — written under `.clips/<token>/` and auto-purged after 2 hours. New `POST /api/library/{id}/clip` + `GET /api/library/clip/{token}/{filename}`. 503 on macOS hosts (no HLS).
- **Docs:** [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md), [docs/API.md](docs/API.md), [docs/FRONTEND.md](docs/FRONTEND.md).

## [4.25.0] — 2026-06-02
- **Improved: offline HLS prep can now run the *entire* transcode on the GPU (decode + scale + encode resident in VRAM), not just the encode.** v4.23.0 moved decode onto NVDEC (`-hwaccel cuda`) but frames still downloaded to system memory and every ABR down-rung was scaled on the CPU — so on a busy ladder the CPU still hovered ~50%. For an **all-encode** ladder (source can't stream-copy) on a `scale_cuda`-capable build with an NVDEC-safe source, `_build_hls_ffmpeg_args` now emits `-hwaccel cuda -hwaccel_output_format cuda -extra_hw_frames 8` and replaces software `scale=-2:H` with `scale_cuda=-2:H:format=yuv420p`, so frames never leave the GPU — eliminating both the per-frame GPU↔CPU copy and the CPU scaling. This targets the worst CPU offender (e.g. h265 season packs that re-encode all three rungs).
  - **Why all-encode only:** mixing a `-c:v copy` rung with `scale_cuda` rungs under `-hwaccel_output_format cuda` **deadlocks ffmpeg** — the copy stream races ahead while the muxer / NVDEC surface pool backs up, wedging at low CPU+GPU with no progress and no exit. The all-GPU path is therefore gated to `not copy_original`; copyable H.264 keeps the proven transparent `-hwaccel cuda` path (cheap copy original + CPU-scaled down-rungs).
  - **Triple-gated:** all-GPU requires `_has_cuda_scale()` (build has the filter), `_source_nvdec_safe()` (h264/hevc/mpeg2/vc1/vp9, 4:2:0 8/10-bit — pinning frames to VRAM removes ffmpeg's SW-decode fallback), and `not copy_original` (no deadlock-prone copy rung). New `_has_cuda_scale()` probe, cached; cleared on ffmpeg install.
  - **Self-recovering from hangs:** a `GPU_STALL_TIMEOUT_SECS=90` watchdog kills the encode if `out_time` stops advancing (a residual cuda deadlock), and `_run_offline_job` then **retries once** on the transparent path — so the GPU pipeline can never leave a file unpreppable or hung. `-extra_hw_frames 8` enlarges the surface pool the parallel `scale_cuda` branches draw from to avoid the stall in the first place.
- **Docs:** [docs/STREAMING.md](docs/STREAMING.md), [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md).

## [4.24.0] — 2026-06-02
- **New: admin "Force Stream Prep" — an on-demand prep that viewers and host activity can't stop.** Overnight / Idle prep are deliberately interruptible (the non-admin Pause control and the activity-kill both halt bulk prep). Force-prep is the opposite: a new **Force Stream Prep** card on Admin → System preps the whole library (or one selected item) for on-device streaming *right now*, and it **runs to completion regardless of the viewer Pause control or live host activity**. Only the admin can stop it.
  - These jobs use a dedicated `"admin"` prep queue. Like interactive (play-on-device) prep they ignore the bulk pause gate (`state.prep_paused`) and the activity-kill (`_pause_prep` / `_activity_kick` only touch `bulk`), and they preempt any in-flight bulk encode. Unlike interactive prep, the admin can halt them.
