Each row has a per-file **Download** link, plus **Download All (.zip)** at the top that streams a deflate-compressed bundle named `streamlink-logs-YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS.zip`. Lets operators pull diagnostics off a remote box (Windows in particular) without needing SSH or Remote Desktop.
- **Backend:** `GET /api/admin/logs` (listing), `GET /api/admin/logs/{name}` (single file, attachment disposition), `GET /api/admin/logs/_bundle` (streaming ZIP via the same `os.pipe()` pattern used by `/api/library/{id}/zip`). All three require admin auth, and `_safe_log_path` rejects any name containing a slash, `..`, an absolute path, or a resolved location outside `LOG_DIR` so the file-by-name endpoint can't be coaxed into reading anything outside `logs/`. The per-file route uses the token via `?admin_token=` query param so plain `<a download>` anchors work (anchor downloads can't set headers).

## [3.5.2] — 2026-05-25
- **Fix: on Windows the YouTube kiosk launched but stayed behind VLC** — the idle background video kept the screen and the kiosk window only flashed in the taskbar until you clicked it. Two causes, both Windows-specific:
  - **Focus-stealing prevention.** The server isn't the foreground process, so the browser window it spawns is denied focus (Windows flashes its taskbar button instead). Now `_bring_tv_to_front` finds the kiosk window **by its title** (`_TV_WINDOW_MARKER` = the `static/tv.html` `<title>`, since Chrome is multi-process so PID matching is unreliable) and forces it forward with the same cocktail used for VLC (zero foreground-lock timeout + synthetic ALT + `AttachThreadInput` + `SetForegroundWindow` + clear taskbar flash), retrying for ~10 s while the window is still being created.
  - **VLC stayed on top.** `/api/youtube` only `pl_stop`ped VLC; its window remained. Now it also **minimizes VLC** (`vlc_minimize`, via `_bring_tv_to_front`). Safe because the return-to-background path (`_play_background_video → vlc_focus_and_fullscreen`) `SW_RESTORE`s it.
  - **The background focus loop no longer fights the kiosk.** `vlc_focus_and_fullscreen` now bails the moment `youtube_active` is set — previously a still-running loop would keep minimizing the kiosk and re-focusing VLC for up to ~24 s after a background session.

## [3.5.1] — 2026-05-25
- **Fix: YouTube-on-TV never started on Windows** (it worked on macOS). The video failed to launch and you'd see the idle background video stop, VLC flash its loading animation, then the background video restart — the tell-tale sign that the kiosk launch failed: `_launch_tv_browser` returned False, so `/api/youtube` hit its 500 path, reset `youtube_active`, and ~3 s later `background_video_loop` reclaimed VLC.
  - **Root cause: browser discovery was too narrow on Windows.** It only checked three hard-coded Program Files paths and silently returned None when Chrome/Edge lived elsewhere — most commonly a **per-user Chrome install under `%LOCALAPPDATA%`**, or Edge at a path the list didn't cover.
  - **Fix:** `_find_chrome` now casts a wide net on Windows — the **`App Paths` registry** (HKCU + HKLM, for `chrome.exe` / `msedge.exe` / `brave.exe` / `chromium.exe`), per-user `%LOCALAPPDATA%`, both `Program Files` trees, and PATH — covering Chrome, **Edge** (preinstalled on Win10/11, so this essentially always resolves), Brave and Chromium. Discovery and launch now **log** what they found / why they failed (`logs/streamlink_app.log`) instead of failing silently.
  - **Plus a health-check:** after launching the kiosk, if the `/tv` page doesn't heartbeat within 12 s (it normally checks in within ~1 s), the server now reports a clear on-screen error — "YouTube didn't start on the TV — the browser failed to open" — instead of silently dropping back to the background video. Catches locked-profile / instant-exit / session-0-service cases too.
  - **CLAUDE.md:** added a top-of-file directive that **Windows is the primary target platform** (then Linux, then macOS) — a feature that works on macOS but not Windows is a bug, not partial success.

## [3.5.0] — 2026-05-25
- **New: play any YouTube link on the TV, controlled from the dashboard.** A red **Play on TV** input now sits at the top of the Search tab — paste a YouTube link (watch, `youtu.be`, Shorts, live, embed, or a bare id) and it opens fullscreen on the TV (the host display) and starts playing.
  - **Plays in a browser, not VLC.** VLC 3.0's bundled `youtube.lua` is broken (it "plays" the watch page for a few seconds, never resolves a title/length, then stops), and yt-dlp-into-VLC adds a fragile dependency and caps at 720p without an audio-slave hack. Instead the video plays in a fullscreen **Chrome kiosk** on the host via the **YouTube IFrame Player API** (`static/tv.html`), so quality/ads/captions all "just work".
  - **Driven by the existing controls.** The footer + fullscreen play/pause, ±10/30 s, scrubber, and volume all route to the TV's YouTube player when it's the active playback (`app.youtube_active` → `POST /api/youtube/control` → SSE `yt_command` → IFrame API). The `/tv` page reports position/duration/title/volume back every second (`POST /api/youtube/tv-state`), mirrored onto the reused display fields so the footer scrubber renders YouTube exactly like a VLC play. Save-to-library, handoff, episode-nav and track menus are hidden in YouTube mode.
  - **Backend:** `POST /api/youtube`, `POST /api/youtube/control`, `POST /api/youtube/tv-state`, `GET /tv`; `_extract_youtube_id`, `_find_chrome` (Chrome → Chromium → Edge, or `_CHROME_BIN`), `_launch_tv_browser` (`--kiosk --app` + `--autoplay-policy=no-user-gesture-required` + an isolated `--user-data-dir`), `_kill_tv_browser` (kills only the kiosk, matched by profile dir). A play hot-swaps the video over SSE if the `/tv` page is already open (heartbeat <6 s), else launches the kiosk; the fresh page autoplays from `?v=<id>`. Stop broadcasts `yt_command:close` and hard-kills the kiosk. `stat_broadcaster` + `background_video_loop` are gated while `youtube_active` so they don't clobber the YouTube state or start the idle background video over it. Not VPN-gated (ordinary HTTPS, not P2P).
  - **Docs:** new [docs/YOUTUBE.md](docs/YOUTUBE.md); API/GOTCHAS/ARCHITECTURE/PLAN updated. New Milestone 21.

## [3.4.5] — 2026-05-25
- **Every VLC call now reuses one keep-alive connection — the actual fix for the ~10 s play/resume stall.** 3.4.3/3.4.4 assumed only the `in_play` *reply* was slow, but the real problem was that **every** VLC HTTP call (status polls included) paid a per-call TCP setup against VLC's tiny, effectively single-threaded HTTP server. Three background loops (`stat_broadcaster`, `vlc_progress_tracker`, `background_video_loop`) each opened a *fresh* `httpx.AsyncClient()`/socket every 2–3 s, plus the multi-command play burst — constantly churning connections, so each call took seconds and the poll-based UI flip/seek from 3.4.4 was still gated on slow polls.
  - New shared `_vlc_http()` persistent `httpx.AsyncClient` (`base_url` + client-level BasicAuth, `connect=2 s`/`read=5 s` timeouts, a 4-connection keep-alive pool with 30 s expiry). All four VLC callers — `vlc()`, `vlc_status()`, `vlc_playlist_uri()`, `_play_background_video()` — route through it; the per-call `async with httpx.AsyncClient()` blocks are gone. Created in `lifespan` and closed on shutdown (mirrors the `qbit` client), lazily rebuilt if needed. A warm connection from the polling loops is almost always already pooled when a play starts, so commands and status reads stay sub-second.

## [3.4.4] — 2026-05-25
- **Play/resume no longer sits on "buffering" for ~10 s while VLC is already playing.** The real culprit (3.4.3 only sped up the seek): the UI flip to "playing" *and* the resume seek were both gated on `await vlc("in_play")` **returning** — and VLC's HTTP reply to `in_play` lags several seconds behind actual playback (which starts in <1 s). Worse, the two `timeout=5.0` calls in that path (volume pre-roll + in_play) added up to the "at least 10 s" you saw.
  - `_library_play_launch` and `_vlc_relaunch_playlist` (prev/next) now fire `in_play` **detached** and detect the real start by polling the lighter `status.json` endpoint (`_vlc_wait_until_ready`, now file-aware so it can't latch onto the *previously* playing file). The "playing" flip and the resume seek both happen the instant VLC is genuinely on the new file — typically well under a second — instead of when `in_play` finally replies.
  - The remaining-episodes enqueue still waits for the `in_play` call to land first (correct playlist order), but that wait is now invisible: you're already watching. The detached `in_play` task is cancelled if the play is superseded, so a slow reply can't resurrect a stale file.

## [3.4.3] — 2026-05-25
- **Resume on VLC now jumps to your spot the instant VLC has the file open — not after a fixed 3 s wait.** Starting a library item with a saved position used to fire the resume seek on a blind `asyncio.sleep(3)` after `in_play`, so on a local file (where VLC opens in well under a second) you sat at 0:00 watching the start for ~3 s before it jumped, and the seek could be dropped entirely if VLC happened to still be opening. `_library_play_launch` now polls VLC via the new `_vlc_wait_until_ready()` helper (state is `playing`/`paused` **and** `length` is known — i.e. the demuxer is up and a seek will actually take) and seeks immediately, with one guarded re-issue if VLC ignored the first seek right at open. The same wait now gates the `resume_mode="prompt"` offer so it appears as soon as playback is live. Resume is now as snappy as poking VLC from a phone remote.
- **Fixed `/api/version` reporting a stale `3.3.0`**, which left the badge (3.4.2) newer than the server's value so the client auto-reload never triggered. `UI_VERSION` is back in sync with the badge.

## [3.4.2] — 2026-05-25
- **StreamLink's core path is now the box's top priority — controls/UI/VLC-control stay responsive under heavy prep.** Lowering ffmpeg (3.4.1) wasn't enough: the server process itself sat at normal priority, so on a saturated box it got starved while separate apps (e.g. a VLC remote talking straight to VLC) stayed snappy — the on-screen volume button lagged.
  - **The server raises its own priority at startup** (`_raise_own_priority`, called first thing in `lifespan`, so both the HTTP and HTTPS uvicorn processes do it): `HIGH_PRIORITY_CLASS` on Windows (no admin needed; REALTIME deliberately avoided), a negative `nice` on POSIX (needs root/CAP_SYS_NICE — the installed service; degrades gracefully otherwise). The server is I/O-bound, so high priority just lets its short request bursts preempt the encoder without hogging the box.
  - **All background CPU work stays below it.** Prep ffmpeg already ran BELOW_NORMAL/`nice` (3.4.1); the Smart-Skip **analyzer** subprocesses (ffmpeg decode, fpcalc, ffprobe) now do too (`analyzer._lp` + `_LOWPRIO_KW`) — without this they'd inherit the server's HIGH priority and re-introduce lag during an analysis. Net effect: server ≫ VLC/qBit (normal) ≫ prep/analyzer (below normal).

## [3.4.1] — 2026-05-25
- **Keep the dashboard responsive while stream-prep runs.** Prep is CPU-heavy, so beyond the warning/pause/overnight controls (3.4.0) the work now actively yields to the rest of the app rather than just relying on the user to pause it.
  - **ffmpeg runs at lowered OS priority on every platform.** Windows already used `BELOW_NORMAL_PRIORITY_CLASS`; POSIX hosts now prepend `nice -n 10` (`_ffmpeg_nice_prefix`, fork-safe vs `preexec_fn`, no-ops if `nice` is missing). The bulk encode yields CPU to the web server's event loop, VLC, and qBit, so the site stays usable.
  - **No synchronous bursts on the event loop.** The recursive `.part`/old-bundle removals and the bundle size calc in `_run_offline_job` are offloaded with `asyncio.to_thread`, and `/prep-all` + the overnight `_enqueue_library_prep` now `await asyncio.sleep(0)` between files (the per-file `_maybe_start_prep_job` is synchronous), so kicking off prep on a large pack/library no longer briefly stalls other requests. All heavy prep work was already off-loop (ffmpeg/ffprobe as subprocesses); this closes the remaining small windows.

## [3.4.0] — 2026-05-25
- **Stream-prep is now interruptible and can run itself overnight.** Preparing files for on-device streaming pegs the host CPU, so the dashboard now warns about it, lets anyone pause/resume the work, and can do the whole library automatically while nobody's watching.
  - **Lag warning (`static/index.html`):** the first time you tap **Prep for Streaming** (per-item) or a per-row **Prep** in a session, a modal explains that the server will get laggy and can become unusable at times, and points at the pause control. Acknowledged once per session. The interactive "play on this device" path is unaffected (no warning — you want it now).
  - **Pause / Resume from the non-admin UI:** the top-right prep indicator (`#globalPrepBar`) gained **Pause** and **Resume** buttons. Pause asks how to handle the file being encoded right now — **Finish current file, then stop** (no wasted work) or **Stop now** (terminates the in-flight ffmpeg for instant relief; that file restarts from scratch on resume, since HLS prep can't checkpoint mid-file). New endpoints `POST /api/offline-prep/pause {kill}` and `POST /api/offline-prep/resume`.
  - **Overnight auto-prep (admin → System tab):** a new **Overnight Stream Prep** panel with an enable toggle, start/end times (windows may cross midnight), timezone, and an **on-end** choice — **Pause until next window** or **Continue until finished**. During the window the server queues every un-prepped library file; at the end it either holds (letting the in-flight file finish) or runs to completion. Backed by the `overnight_prep_loop` background task and `GET/POST /api/admin/overnight-prep`; config persists under `library.json → settings.overnight_prep`.
  - **Backend model (`main.py`):** bulk/per-item/overnight prep jobs are tagged `queue:"bulk"` and honor a global pause gate in `_run_offline_job`; a paused bulk job releases the single concurrency slot (so an on-demand play-on-device prep can still run) and is re-spawned on resume. `/api/offline-active`, `/prep-status` and `state_snapshot` now expose paused state for the UI.

## [3.3.0] — 2026-05-25
- **Stream-to-device HLS now ships an adaptive-bitrate ladder + an in-player quality menu.** Each bundle previously carried a single video rendition at source resolution, so a weak LAN/Wi-Fi link had no fallback and there was no way to pick a quality. Bundles now emit **Original + 720p + 480p** (each rung capped at the source height — a ≤480p source still gets one rendition, a 720p source gets Original + 480p), all sharing one audio group so switching quality never re-fetches audio.
  - **Player (`static/index.html`):** the on-device player gains a **Res** dropdown (next to Aud/Sub) populated from hls.js `levels` — `Auto` plus each resolution. `Auto` keeps hls.js adapting to bandwidth; a manual pick sets `hls.currentLevel`. Quality is session-only (not persisted). Safari native HLS auto-adapts among the variants but exposes no reliable manual-level API, so its Res row stays hidden (auto-only).
  - **Backend (`main.py`):** `_build_hls_ffmpeg_args` maps the source video once per ladder rung and sets per-output codec/scale (`scale=-2:<h>`, with `maxrate`/`bufsize` VBV caps for realistic master-playlist BANDWIDTH). The original rung still stream-copies when the source is browser-safe H.264 — even when NVENC is present — and only the scaled down-rungs transcode (NVENC on GPU when available, else libx264). `meta.json` and the `offline-prepare` response gain a `videos[]` array.
  - **`OFFLINE_CACHE_VERSION` → `v7-hls-abr`** so existing single-rendition `v6-hls` bundles rebuild on next prep/play; old dirs surface as orphans in Admin → Offline Cache for purge.
  - **Trade-offs:** down-rungs always transcode (slower prep; much faster with NVENC) and bundle storage grows ~1.6–1.9×.

## [3.2.2] — 2026-05-24
- **Bug fix (Windows): `fragLoadError` on `init_video.mp4 → HTTP 404` — the v3.2.1 fix was incomplete.** The new diagnostic alert pinpointed it: the fmp4 init segment 404s on a Windows host. Pinning `-hls_fmp4_init_filename "init_%v.mp4"` fixed the *name* but not the *location*. ffmpeg derives the init segment's output directory by parsing the **playlist** path; on Windows that path has backslashes, the parse fails, and the init file gets written to the server's working directory instead of the bundle `.part/` dir — so it never makes it into the cache and 404s at playback. (A full path on the init arg isn't an option — ffmpeg prepends the playlist dir to it and the encode dies with "Failed to open segment".)
  - **Fix:** every ffmpeg **output** is now a bare filename (init / segments / playlists / subs) and the subprocess runs with `cwd=<bundle .part dir>`, so they all land in the bundle on every OS regardless of path separators. The `-i` source stays absolute. `_build_hls_ffmpeg_args` no longer takes `out_dir`.
  - **`OFFLINE_CACHE_VERSION` → `v6-hls`** so the (still-broken) `v5-hls` bundles from the previous attempt rebuild on next prep/play.

## [3.2.1] — 2026-05-24
- **Bug fix: HLS playback never started — manifest + subtitle/audio dropdowns loaded, then a fatal `fragLoadError` and a black player.** The bundle's manifest and per-rendition playlists fetched fine (so `MANIFEST_PARSED` fired and the dropdowns populated), but the very first media fetch failed. Root cause: `_build_hls_ffmpeg_args` templated every bundle filename *except* the fmp4 init segment, leaving `-hls_fmp4_init_filename` at ffmpeg's default. ffmpeg's own `%v` expansion for the init segment doesn't always match the `#EXT-X-MAP:URI=` it writes into each variant playlist, so the player requested an init segment that didn't exist on disk → 404 → hls.js retried, gave up, and emitted a fatal `fragLoadError` before a single frame decoded.
  - **Fix:** pin `-hls_fmp4_init_filename "init_%v.mp4"` so the init files (`init_video.mp4`, `init_audio_0.mp4`, …) follow the same `name:`-tag scheme as the segments (`seg_video_…`, `seg_audio_0_…`) and the `EXT-X-MAP` URI matches the file on disk on every ffmpeg ≥ 4.3.
  - **`OFFLINE_CACHE_VERSION` → `v5-hls`** so existing (broken) bundles rebuild on next prep/play; old `v4-hls` dirs surface as orphans in Admin → Offline Cache for purge.
  - **Player diagnostics:** the hls.js `ERROR` handler now logs the failing URL + HTTP status to the console and includes the segment name + code in the on-screen alert, so any residual "won't play" is self-diagnosing instead of a bare `fragLoadError`.

## [3.2.0] — 2026-05-20
- **Fix: HLS stream-to-device never worked when the source had subtitles (i.e. essentially always).** The new `logs/hls.log` revealed the real failure: `ffmpeg ... Could not write header ... No streams to mux were specified ... Conversion failed!`. Reproduced locally on the same ffmpeg 8.1.1 — ffmpeg's HLS muxer **cannot** package multi-track WebVTT into a manifest. A single inline subtitle works; two or more (declared as their own `s:N,sgroup:…` variants, as we did) fail unconditionally, for both `fmp4` and `mpegts` segment types. Since virtually every release MKV has many subtitle tracks, HLS prep aborted on every real file.
  - **`_build_hls_ffmpeg_args` rearchitected:** the HLS bundle is now **video + audio only** (fmp4, unchanged and working). Each text subtitle is emitted as a standalone `sub_<i>.vtt` **sidecar** in the same single ffmpeg pass (`-map 0:s:N -c:s webvtt -f webvtt sub_N.vtt`). `meta.json` subtitle entries now carry `file: "sub_<i>.vtt"` instead of an in-manifest `playlist`.
  - **Player (`static/index.html`):** bundle subtitles are wired as `<track>` children of `<video>` exactly like on-disk sidecar subs, unifying the two code paths. `_lpApplySubIdx` now toggles `track.mode` by dropdown key across both the hls.js and Safari-native paths (the old `hls.subtitleTrack` route is gone). New `lp.subTracks` records every created `<track>` in dropdown order.
  - **`OFFLINE_CACHE_VERSION` → `v4-hls`** so any previously-(failed/partial) bundles rebuild on next prep; old `v3-hls` dirs surface as orphans in Admin → Offline Cache.
- **Stream-to-device marked unavailable on macOS hosts.** ffmpeg/ffprobe run as children of the (non-GUI) server process, and macOS TCC blocks them from reading media in the user's protected `~/Downloads` / `~/Desktop` / `~/Documents` — every prep aborts at the probe step with `Operation not permitted` (VLC/qBit work because they're separate, individually-granted apps). The prep endpoints now return a clear 503 (`offline_prepare`) / error (`_maybe_start_prep_job`, `_run_offline_job`) on Darwin, `state_snapshot` exposes `hls_available`, and the UI hides every Prep / On-Device affordance (and routes the play chooser straight to VLC) via a `no-hls` body class.

## [3.1.0] — 2026-05-20
- **Minor feature: real logging for the backend, focused on the HLS offline-prep pipeline.** `main.py` had no `logging` setup at all — background-task failures (most painfully an HLS conversion that died seconds after starting) were swallowed into a 500-char `job["error"]` tail with nothing written to disk, leaving operators no way to find out *why*.
  - **New logger config (`_init_logging`)** wires up a `streamlink` logger with two rotating file handlers — `logs/streamlink_app.log` (everything) and `logs/hls.log` (HLS only, via the `streamlink.hls` child logger) — at 2 MB × 3 backups each, plus a stderr handler capped at `WARNING` so a bulk `/prep-all` doesn't bury the interactive console while the full INFO trail still lands on disk. Idempotent across reloads; `propagate=False` avoids double-logging through uvicorn's root.
  - **`_run_offline_job` instrumented end to end:** logs job START (src/out), the exact ffmpeg command line (shell-quoted), encoder choice + track counts, and DONE (elapsed + bundle size). Every abort path — ffmpeg missing, ffmpeg too old, no video stream — now logs at ERROR. On a non-zero ffmpeg exit it logs the **return code, elapsed time, full command, and the last 300 lines of ffmpeg stderr** to `logs/hls.log` (the UI keeps its short tail). The outer handler uses `hls_log.exception` so crashes carry a traceback.
  - **Latent deadlock fixed as part of the stderr capture:** ffmpeg's stderr is now drained concurrently into a bounded buffer instead of being read only after `proc.wait()`. A chatty ffmpeg could previously fill the OS pipe buffer and block on write while we waited on it — `proc.wait()` would hang forever. Draining as output arrives both prevents that and gives us the complete error to log.

## [3.0.0] — 2026-05-18
- **Major feature: multi-track Stream-to-Device via HLS.** The local-device player now exposes every audio track and every text subtitle from the source MKV, with runtime switching that works across every modern browser. End-to-end rewrite of the offline-prep pipeline.
  - **Backend:** `_run_offline_job` rewritten to emit per-source HLS bundles (`<sha>/master.m3u8` + per-rendition `.m3u8` + fmp4 segments + `meta.json`) instead of single MP4s. One ffmpeg invocation with `-var_stream_map` maps the video, every audio track (each transcoded to AAC stereo at 160 kbps), and every text subtitle (transcoded to WebVTT). Image-based subs (PGS / VOBSUB / DVB) are filtered out by `_ffprobe_full` and reported in `meta.json:skipped_image_subs`. Video stream-copies when the source is already H.264 yuv420p with a non-Hi10P profile; otherwise transcodes via libx264 (or h264_nvenc when available). ffmpeg ≥ 4.3 is now required and enforced via `_ffmpeg_version()` cache — older builds fail-fast with a clear error before launching the encode.
  - **Cache layout:** `OFFLINE_CACHE_VERSION` bumped to `v3-hls`. Cache key is the same `sha256(VERSION|path|mtime|size)[:24]` but now keys a directory (`<sha>/`) instead of a file (`<sha>.mp4`). The old single-MP4 caches map to different keys under v3 and surface as `kind: "legacy"` orphans in Admin → Offline Cache for one-click purge. Per-source storage: bundle ≈ source size + AAC stereo per audio track (a 4 GB BD remux with 3 audios ≈ 4.7 GB vs. 4 GB before).
  - **Endpoints:** `/api/library/offline-cache/{name}` replaced with `/api/library/offline-cache/{cache_key}/{filename}` — strict regex validation on both segments (`[a-f0-9]{24}` + `[A-Za-z0-9._-]+`) prevents path traversal. `/offline-prepare` now returns `master_url` + `audios[]` + `subtitles[]` + `saved_tracks{}` instead of `video_url`. New `POST /api/library/{id}/local-tracks` persists the in-browser player's audio/subtitle picks per-profile per-file as `local_audio_idx` / `local_subtitle_idx` — kept separate from VLC's `audio_track` / `subtitle_track` (ES IDs) which use a different addressing scheme. `update_progress` and `mark_watched` preserve all four track-pref keys across writes.
  - **Admin Offline Cache tab** now walks directories: `_dir_size_bytes` recurses into each `<sha>/` for accurate per-item totals; `_delete_cache_artifacts` removes the bundle dir + any `.part/` staging dir + any legacy MP4 in one operation; the orphan list now includes a `legacy` kind for pre-v3 single-MP4 caches.
  - **Frontend:** ships `static/vendor/hls.min.js` (hls.js v1.5.17, ~100 KB gzipped) bundled locally — lazy-loaded on first local-player open via `_ensureHlsLib()` so the dashboard's initial paint isn't delayed. `_lpLoadIndex` rewritten to branch on `Hls.isSupported()`: hls.js for Chrome / Firefox / Edge / Android Chrome (MSE-based), `<video>.src = master_url` for Safari (native HLS). Audio/sub dropdowns populated from the bundle's `meta.json`; sidecar `.srt`/`.vtt` files coexist with bundle subs as additional dropdown options (using a `"sidecar:N"` index sentinel). `lpSetAudio(idx)` and `lpSetSubtitle(idx)` switch tracks at runtime via `hls.audioTrack` / `hls.subtitleTrack` on hls.js or `AudioTrackList.enabled` / `TextTrackList.mode` on Safari. Each switch POSTs to `/local-tracks` so the pick comes back on next play. Local-player markup gains an `lpAudioRow` next to `lpSubRow`; the row container is hidden when there's exactly one audio track and zero subtitles.
  - **UX trade-offs documented in [docs/GOTCHAS.md](docs/GOTCHAS.md):** segment-boundary seek granularity (~6 s, mostly invisible), ASS/SSA styling loss in WebVTT conversion (libass.js render-on-canvas is the deferred fix), image-based subs skipped entirely (PGS / VOBSUB / DVB — use VLC for those), audio always downmixed to AAC stereo (5.1 preservation needs the VLC path), local-player and VLC track prefs intentionally independent.
  - **Migration:** existing `.offline_cache/*.mp4` files orphan immediately; users need to re-prep their library after upgrade. Admin → Offline Cache → Purge All clears them in one click.

## [2.11.0] — 2026-05-24
- **Minor feature: re-running setup pre-fills your current `.env` values (and doubles as a config health check).** Previously the "Existing .env detected" prompt was all-or-nothing — reuse everything untouched, or re-prompt from scratch with the factory defaults, forcing you to retype every setting (Jackett URL, qBit/VLC passwords, etc.) just to change one. Now choosing to re-prompt pre-fills each field with the value currently in `.env`, so you can press Enter to keep any setting and only type over the ones you want to change. Walking through the prompts now also surfaces every active value, so it works as a quick way to audit the config before, say, re-running setup to apply the Jackett auto-recovery grant.
  - **`gather_config(existing)`** ([setup.py](setup.py)) takes the parsed existing `.env` and defaults each prompt to the stored value, falling back to the factory default on a fresh install (unchanged first-run behaviour).
  - **Secrets are never echoed.** Stored passwords (`JACKETT_PASSWORD`, `QBIT_PASSWORD`, `VLC_PASSWORD`, `ADMIN_PASSWORD`) show a masked `•••••• (Enter = keep)` hint instead of the plaintext value, so re-running setup can't leak them to the terminal/scrollback; pressing Enter still keeps the stored value, and a currently-blank secret shows `(currently blank)`. `ask()` gained a `show_default` override to support this.

## [2.10.1] — 2026-05-23
- **Bug fix: `remote.local` stops resolving after a reboot when run as a system service.** Root cause: the installed service registered mDNS exactly once at startup, but at boot it launches before Wi-Fi has associated and the interface has a LAN IP. `get_local_ip()` returned `""`, so the registration was silently skipped — `remote.local` then never resolved until the next manual relaunch, even though uvicorn (bound to `0.0.0.0`) became reachable by IP the moment the network came up. That's why it worked on first interactive install (network already up) but not after a reboot.
  - **`start_mdns_resilient()` (in `run.py`).** Registers mDNS from a background daemon thread that polls `get_local_ip()` until a LAN IP appears, registers `remote.local`, then re-registers if the IP later changes (DHCP lease, network switch). Polls every 5 s until registered, then every 30 s to watch for changes. Returns a `.close()` handle for shutdown cleanup.
  - **Used by both launch paths.** The generated service wrapper (`daemon.py`) and interactive `run.py` both now call `start_mdns_resilient()` instead of the one-shot `start_mdns()`, keeping them behaviourally identical and fixing the same latent issue when `run.py` is launched before Wi-Fi.
  - **Re-run `python3 run.py --install` to regenerate the service wrapper** with the fix.

## [2.10.0] — 2026-05-23
- **Minor feature: machine reboot + scheduled daily restart (Jackett hard-reset).** A reboot is the only reliable cure for some wedged-Jackett states, so the admin **System** tab now exposes both a manual reboot and an automated nightly one.
  - **Reboot Machine.** New `POST /api/admin/reboot` restarts the whole host (not just the web server). `_reboot_machine()` tries platform-appropriate commands in order — macOS: System Events restart (no sudo from a launchd user agent) → `sudo -n shutdown -r now` → `shutdown -r now`; Linux: `systemctl reboot` → `sudo -n shutdown` → `shutdown`; Windows: `shutdown /r /t 0`. Fires ~0.5 s after the response flushes so the UI gets confirmation first.
  - **Scheduled Restart.** New `scheduled_reboot_loop` background task + `GET`/`POST /api/admin/scheduled-reboot`. Config (`enabled`, `time` HH:MM, `timezone`, `idle_minutes`) persists under `library.json → settings.scheduled_reboot`. At the configured local time (default 00:00 America/Los_Angeles) it checks whether the box was used in the last `idle_minutes`; if idle it reboots, otherwise it waits `idle_minutes` and re-checks, repeating until idle. A persisted `last_fired` date guards against the just-rebooted machine immediately re-arming and looping.
  - **Idle detection.** New `track_activity` middleware stamps `state.last_activity` on mutating requests + search (routine GET polling is ignored). `_machine_in_use()` also treats live VLC playback/pause of non-background content and any active stream/download as "in use", so a reboot never interrupts active watching or a running download.
  - **Auto-recovery requirement.** For the host to come back after a reboot, the user must configure OS auto-login and install the StreamLink system service (`run.py --install`). Documented in the README and the System tab.

## [2.9.0] — 2026-05-20
- **Jackett reliability: detect and recover a hung indexer instead of needing a reboot.** Root cause of "Jackett stops working after a while, only a reboot fixes it": the watchdog's liveness check was a bare TCP port-open, and a hung Jackett keeps its listener socket bound while it stops serving HTTP — so the watchdog thought it was healthy and never restarted it. Even when it did try, `sc.exe start Jackett` is a no-op (1056 ALREADY_RUNNING) on a wedged service, so only a reboot cleared it.
  - **HTTP health check.** The watchdog, `run.py` startup, and a new in-app monitor now probe `GET {INDEXER_URL}/UI/Login` (any HTTP status proves the web stack is alive) via `_http_ok()` instead of a port check. `ServiceSpec` grew a `health_check` hook; `is_alive()` uses it for Jackett (VLC/qBit unchanged), and `start()` waits on it so a restart doesn't tight-loop before Jackett finishes warming up.
  - **Force-down before restart.** A new `pre_restart` hook force-stops the wedged Jackett (`sc stop` + wait for STOPPED, hard-kill fallback; `kill_by_name` off-Windows) before relaunching, so the port frees and the restart actually takes. When no `Jackett` service exists, the watchdog now launches the tray/console exe as a user process instead of giving up.
  - **Permission grant so a non-elevated watchdog can recover the service.** A LocalSystem `Jackett` service can only be `sc` stopped/started by an admin — the reason a non-elevated StreamLink hit a UAC/access-denied wall. `setup.py`'s new `grant_jackett_service_control()` additively grants Authenticated Users `SERVICE_START`+`SERVICE_STOP` via `sc sdset` and sets `sc failure` auto-restart actions (idempotent, best-effort, one UAC prompt; prints the manual commands if elevation is declined). Re-run `setup.py` to apply. Access-denied paths now log an actionable hint.
  - **In-app catch-safe + visibility.** New `jackett_health_monitor` background task polls every 20 s, publishes `state.jackett_ok` (in `state_snapshot()`) and a `jackett_status` SSE event, and — only after ~2 min of sustained local outage (i.e. when no watchdog has recovered it) — calls the reusable `watchdog.restart_jackett()` as a backstop, so it never duels a healthy watchdog.

## [2.8.0] — 2026-05-19
- **Minor feature: bidirectional Handoff (TV ⇄ device), time-synced.**
  - **TV → device.** While a library item is playing on the TV (VLC), a new emerald **Device** button (next to Stop in the player footer, and a **To Device** tile next to Stop in the fullscreen controls) hands playback to the browser that tapped it. Both require a **0.5 s hold** to activate (same `_holdStart` / `.hold-btn` progress-fill pattern as Stop), so an accidental tap can't yank playback off the TV. It captures VLC's live position via a fresh `GET /api/vlc/tracks` read, starts the local `<video>` player on the same item — using the remaining-playlist tail so auto-advance keeps going — seeked to that exact time, and stops VLC. `/api/stop` returns 202, so the device's prep/transcode runs in parallel with the TV tearing down; the resume seek is frozen at the captured time, so the handoff lands on the same frame regardless of how long prep takes. The button shows only during library playback (`is_library_playback && library_item_id`) and is gated by `withInflight("handoff")` against double-taps. To support it, `state_snapshot()` now also publishes `library_item_id` and the full ordered `library_playlist`, and the frontend `app` mirrors both.
  - **Prep gating.** The handoff-to-device button is greyed out with a "Not prepped for on-device streaming" note (footer: tooltip; fullscreen tile: visible sub-label) when the currently-playing file has no `.offline_cache` MP4 and isn't Safari-native — handing off then would stop the TV and drop into a long transcode. Readiness is resolved from `prepFileState` (instant when known) and a per-file `GET /api/library/{id}/prep-status` check (`_handoffReadyState` / `_maybeRefreshHandoffReady`), and the button flips to active automatically once the file is prepped (via the episode picker's Prep / a card's Prep for Streaming). Tapping it while not prepped shows a toast instead of acting.
  - **Device → TV.** The on-device local player now has the mirror-image **To TV** button in its fullscreen header (next to Stop): `lpHandoffToVlc` captures the `<video>` position + remaining playlist tail, tears down the device player (flushing progress), and starts VLC playback at the exact same time via `playLibraryFiles` (`POST /api/library/{id}/play` with `seek_first_to`). Gated by `withInflight("handoff_vlc")`.

## [2.7.0] — 2026-05-19
- **Minor feature: the auto-skip countdown now runs *before* the skip point, and the intro/credits is skipped in full.** Previously the countdown started *at* the intro/credits start and skipped N seconds later, so the first 5 s of an intro (or 10 s of credits) played first. Now the countdown leads *into* the skip point — e.g. for an intro starting at 1:30 the 5-second countdown runs 1:25→1:30 and the skip fires exactly at 1:30, so none of the intro plays. Credits likewise count down over the 10 s before `credits_start` and advance to the next episode the moment credits begin. The countdown is now **position-driven** (`_run_skip_countdown` shows `ceil(target − pos)` and fires at `pos ≥ target`), so it tracks real playback: it freezes while paused and follows seeks, polling every 0.5 s so the popup clears within ~0.5 s when you scrub out of the window. The auto trigger window widened to `[skip_point − lead, …)`; the manual (auto-skip-off) Skip button is unchanged.

## [2.6.2] — 2026-05-19
- **Bug fix:** The countdown popup ("Skipping intro in 1") stayed frozen on the TV after the skip fired — and after any seek that ended the countdown. Root cause: VLC's `marq` filter reads `--marq-file` with `getdelim()`, which returns EOF on an *empty* file, so the filter **keeps the previously-rendered text** instead of blanking it (and logs a read error every refresh tick). Every "clear" wrote an empty string, which was a no-op on screen. `_marquee_write` now clears by writing a single space — a valid non-empty line that forces marq to update but renders no glyph (we draw no background box). `run.py` / `watchdog.py` likewise seed the file with a space, not "". This is what actually made 2.6.1's two-sided-window abort visible on screen.

## [2.6.1] — 2026-05-19
- **Bug fix:** The "Skipping intro in N" countdown popup no longer lingers when the viewer scrubs the progress bar past the intro. `_run_skip_countdown` previously only aborted when the position moved *below* the window floor (a backward seek); a forward seek out of the intro left the popup up and would have yanked playback back to the intro end when the count hit zero. The countdown now takes a `[floor, ceil)` window (intro `ceil = intro end`; credits unbounded) and aborts on leaving it in **either** direction, clearing the popup within ~1 s of the seek.

## [2.6.0] — 2026-05-19
- **Minor feature: on-TV auto-skip countdown popup.** When a profile has auto-skip enabled, Smart Skip no longer cuts instantly — it first shows a countdown directly on the TV (VLC) before acting: **10 s** before auto-advancing past credits, **5 s** before seeking past an intro. The popup renders bottom-right with padding, as opaque white text. Implemented via a VLC `marq` sub-source: VLC is launched (in `run.py`, `watchdog.py`, and `main.py`'s `_restart_vlc_process`) with `--sub-source=marq --marq-file=<repo>/.vlc_marquee.txt --marq-position=10 …`, and `main.py` writes "Skipping intro/credits in N" into that file each second (emptying it clears the popup). Text-only — no global freetype background box — so regular subtitles render unchanged. A dedicated countdown coroutine (`_run_skip_countdown`) polls VLC each tick so it holds while paused and aborts if the viewer seeks out of the window or switches files; Stop / Next / Prev / a new Play all cancel it and wipe the popup. New `state.skip_countdown` field is included in the SSE state snapshot.

## [2.5.0] — 2026-05-18
- **Minor feature: automatic UI cache-bust on version mismatch.** Added `GET /api/version` (returns `{"version": "…"}` with `no-cache` headers) and a `UI_VERSION` constant in `main.py` that must be kept in sync with the version badge in `index.html`. On every page load, a self-invoking script block reads the version baked into the loaded HTML (via the `[data-ui-version]` badge) and compares it against the server response. If the cached page is older than the server's version, the page reloads with a `?_v=<version>` cache-busting query parameter so the browser fetches the updated HTML. A `sessionStorage` guard prevents infinite reload loops.

## [2.4.4] — 2026-05-18
- **Bug fix:** New clients no longer see "No active stream" when they open the remote while VLC is in the middle of real playback — the dashboard now reconciles `state` with VLC on startup. Trigger was a `uvicorn main:app` restart (admin Shut Down, watchdog kick, manual relaunch) while VLC kept running: every `AppState` field reset to its dataclass default (`stream_status="idle"`, `active_title=None`), and `background_video_loop` saw VLC already `state=playing` so it stayed out of the way — leaving every SSE client stuck on "No active stream" until someone pressed Stop and started over. New `_sync_state_from_vlc()` runs in `lifespan` after the volume init: queries `status.json` + `playlist.json`, matches the currently-playing URI against the background-video path (→ sets `background_playing=True` and returns) or every library item's files (→ seeds `active_title`, `library_item_id`, `library_playlist`, `library_current_file`, `active_hash`), and falls back to using the file stem as the title for un-matched playback (external VLC plays, stream-now items whose torrent has been GC'd from `library.json`). `library_profile_id` is intentionally left unset — the original profile isn't recoverable, so `vlc_progress_tracker` skips progress saves and skip offers for the restored session, but title display and next/prev/stop work normally.

## [2.4.3] — 2026-05-18
- **Bug fix:** On server restart, the default VLC volume is now half of the configured max-volume cap instead of 100 (normal). `lifespan` reads the cap from `library.json` settings, sets `state.vlc_volume` and `state.user_volume_before_bg` to `cap // 2`, and immediately pushes that value to VLC. This prevents an audio blast when playback starts on a fresh server start — the pre-existing `vlc("in_play")` pre-roll already sends the volume before any media loads, so the correct starting level now flows through cleanly.

## [2.4.2] — 2026-05-18
- **Bug fix:** Button text is no longer selectable. Added `user-select: none; -webkit-user-select: none` to the global `button, select` rule in `index.html` and a matching `button` rule in `admin.html`.

## [2.4.1] — 2026-05-18
- **Bug fix:** Profile-picker bottom buttons (**Log in with PIN**, **Manage profiles**, **Admin**) are no longer covered by playback chrome on mobile when a video is playing. The picker is `fixed inset-0 z-40` with `bg-gray-950`, but the player footer is also `z-40` and later in the DOM, and the skip/resume offers and local-device player sit at `z-50`+, so all of them bled through over the picker's bottom row on short viewports. Added a `body:has(#profilePicker:not(.hidden))` rule that hides `footer`, `#skipOffer`, `#resumeOffer`, and `#localPlayer` while the picker is up — turns the picker into a proper lock-screen overlay regardless of what's playing in the background.

## [2.4.0] — 2026-05-18
- **Minor feature: Shut Down Server from the admin panel.** New **System** tab in `/admin` with a single red "Shut Down" button. Posts to a new `POST /api/admin/shutdown` endpoint, which enumerates every `uvicorn main:app` process via psutil and sends SIGTERM — siblings first (so the admin process can finish issuing signals), self last, with a 3 s `os._exit(0)` fallback if uvicorn ignores the signal. Once the HTTP uvicorn exits, `run.py`'s existing `finally` block tears down the HTTPS sibling and the mDNS responder. qBittorrent / Jackett / VLC are not touched — they aren't children of the FastAPI process. Useful for stopping the server cleanly from a phone without SSH-ing into the host.

## [2.3.0] — 2026-05-18
- **Minor feature: hold-to-activate on destructive / navigation controls.** The footer Stop button, the footer Prev / Next episode buttons, and the fullscreen-overlay Stop / Prev / Next tiles now require a 0.5 s press-and-hold to fire instead of a single tap. A short tap is a no-op. While held, a CSS fill grows left-to-right across the button so the user can see the timer counting, then briefly flashes once the action fires. Backed by a generic `_holdStart` / `_holdCancel` helper that wires `pointerdown` / `pointerup` / `pointerleave` / `pointercancel` — works on touch and mouse. Motivation: these three controls all kick the user out of their current playback context, and an accidental brush against the bottom strip was triggering them.
- **Retry button removed.** The amber "Retry" tile in the fullscreen controls (added in 4.4 as a workaround for VLC freezes when files weren't ready) has been removed along with its frontend `retryPlayback` handler. The `/api/retry` endpoint and `_retry_task` helper in `main.py` are kept in place for now in case they're useful via direct API; they're no longer reachable from the UI.

## [2.2.1] — 2026-05-18
- **Bug fix:** Player UI no longer gets stuck on "Loading…" / buffering after a library play, even though VLC is already playing. The 2.2.0 refactor of `/api/library/{id}/play` flipped `state.stream_status` to `"playing"` only *after* the full `in_play` + sequential `in_enqueue` loop completed — so a "continue watching" play that enqueued 50+ remaining episodes left the UI in buffering for many seconds even though VLC had been playing the first episode from the start. The state flip + broadcast now run the instant VLC accepts the first track (the only roundtrip that gates actual playback), and the remaining `in_enqueue` calls run in parallel via `asyncio.gather` so wall time is one roundtrip max regardless of playlist length. Same fix applied to `/api/vlc/prev` and `/api/vlc/next`'s `_vlc_relaunch_playlist` helper.

## [2.2.0] — 2026-05-18
- **Minor feature: slow-network playback responsiveness.** On a slow or flaky link the app used to feel dead for several seconds between "user clicks Play" and "VLC actually opens the file" — the Play response was synchronous on the VLC HTTP roundtrips, the chooser modal closed immediately, and the player UI didn't paint until the SSE `playing` event arrived. Four-part fix:
  1. **Server: non-blocking playback handoff.** `/api/library/{id}/play`, `/api/vlc/prev`, `/api/vlc/next`, `/api/stop`, and `/api/stream` now broadcast a state event (`buffering` / `idle`) and return 202 immediately. The slow VLC `in_play` + `in_enqueue` work (and the qBit deletes on stop/stream) run in background tasks so the response no longer waits on the network at all. A new `state.library_play_task` is tracked and cancelled on subsequent Play / Stop so a slow handoff can't race a newer action.
  2. **Client: optimistic buffering UI.** A new `_optimisticBuffering(label, itemId)` helper flips `app.stream_status` to `buffering`, populates `active_title` from the cached library item, and opens the mobile fullscreen overlay the instant the user clicks Play — no waiting for the server. `renderPlayer` now also auto-opens the overlay on `stream_status === "buffering"` (previously only on `playing`). For library plays the buffering badge says **"Loading…"** and the fullscreen status says **"Starting playback…"** (instead of the misleading "Buffering…" / "Connecting…" copy, which made fully-downloaded episodes look like network problems).
  3. **Client: in-flight guards on Play.** `continueLibraryItem` and `playLibraryFiles` now run under `withInflight("play_${itemId}", …)`, so an impatient double-tap while the server is mid-handoff is dropped client-side instead of racing extra `in_play` requests to VLC. They also bail with a warn-toast if `app._connected === false` (i.e. SSE has been disconnected past the 4 s grace), since the response would otherwise never get a confirming state event.
  4. **Client: visible SSE connection state.** The navbar's SSE pill (`#sseLabel`) now shows **LIVE** / **OFFLINE** on mobile too (previously `hidden sm:block`), and after a 4 s reconnect grace the user gets a "Lost connection to host — reconnecting…" toast plus a guard that blocks new Play actions until SSE re-opens.

## [2.1.8] — 2026-05-17
- **Bug fix:** Resume popup now resumes playback in the same mode that is already active (VLC if no local player is open, local device player if it is), instead of always opening the "Play where?" chooser.

## [2.1.7] — 2026-05-17
- **Bug fix:** Fullscreen-controls overlay no longer lets users highlight (text-select) any of its labels, buttons, title, or time readout when long-pressing or drag-selecting on touch / desktop. Previously only `.fc-tile` elements had `user-select:none`; now the entire `#fullscreenControls` subtree disables selection and the iOS tap-highlight flash.

## [2.1.6] — 2026-05-17
- **Bug fix:** Idle background video now reliably comes up fullscreen with the taskbar / Dock hidden and every other app minimized when StreamLink is launched as a system service at boot/login. Three-part fix:
  1. VLC is now spawned with `--fullscreen` in all three launch paths (`run.py`, `watchdog.py`, `main.py:_restart_vlc_process`) so it owns the screen from the very first frame instead of relying on a post-`in_play` HTTP toggle.
  2. `vlc_focus_and_fullscreen` no longer runs the focus + minimize-others pass once — it now loops for ~24 s on a slowing cadence (6× 0.5 s, 8× 1 s, 6× 2 s), re-asserting focus and re-minimizing every visible non-VLC window each iteration. The previous one-shot pass only caught apps that were already visible at the moment vlc_focus_and_fullscreen ran, and startup apps that launch a few seconds *after* logon would appear on top of VLC and leave the taskbar / Dock visible. The Stop-button path didn't have this problem because the desktop is already settled when Stop is pressed; the loop replicates that "stable desktop" condition for the boot path.
  3. On macOS the focus path additionally hides every other visible app via AppleScript so the player covers the screen — the counterpart to the existing Windows `_minimize_other_windows_windows` call.

## [2.1.5] — 2026-05-17
- **Bug fix:** Setup and launcher prompts no longer hang when stdin is non-interactive (system service, piped invocation, etc.). `setup.py`'s `ask`/`ask_bool` now check `sys.stdin.isatty()` upfront and auto-apply the default if there's no console — previously they relied on `input()` raising `EOFError`, which does not always fire reliably under Windows Task Scheduler. The `.env`-reuse prompt now correctly defaults to "yes" in service contexts. `run.py`'s "Continue without VPN?" prompt is similarly gated and silently proceeds when non-interactive (safe because the watchdog already gates qBittorrent on VPN status).

## [2.1.4] — 2026-05-16
- **Bug fix (Windows):** Dropped `/RL HIGHEST` from the scheduled task created by `run.py --install`. On Windows, ports below 1024 do not require admin to bind (the "privileged ports" rule is Unix-only), so the wrapper doesn't need elevation. HIGHEST was actively harmful for Standard User accounts — it made Task Scheduler try to elevate their token at trigger time, which failed silently and left the task registered but never running. Firewall rules (which DO need admin) are now added during `_windows_install` while we hold the UAC-granted admin token.
- **Setup warning:** `setup.py` now detects per-user Python installs on Windows (Microsoft Store python, `AppData\Local\Programs\Python`, etc.) and warns that the resulting venv will not be usable by any other Windows user account. This was the silent root cause of the service-doesn't-run case: when the scheduled task ran as a different user, the venv launcher couldn't read the base python in the installer's user profile and bailed with "Access is denied" before the wrapper could log anything.
- **Docs:** New GOTCHAS entries for Microsoft Store Python and the `/RL HIGHEST` / `/RU` Windows-task pitfalls so the next person doesn't have to re-debug.

## [2.1.3] — 2026-05-16
- **Bug fix (Windows):** `run.py --install` now registers the scheduled task to run as the *console* user (the one actually sitting at the keyboard), not the Admin account whose credentials were entered at the UAC prompt. Previously, installing from an elevated Admin shell while logged in as a regular user would tie the task to the Admin's logon, so the task never fired at the user's logon — the service appeared to install successfully but never started, with no logs written. Detection uses `WTSGetActiveConsoleSessionId` + `WTSQuerySessionInformationW` (works on all Windows editions), with a PowerShell `Win32_ComputerSystem.UserName` fallback. Install output now prints the detected `RunAs` user so it's clear which account the service is tied to.

## [2.1.2] — 2026-05-16
- **Bug fix:** System service (`run.py --install`) now registers mDNS, opens Windows firewall, and launches the HTTPS admin process — matching what `python run.py` does interactively. Previously the service only ran the watchdog + HTTP uvicorn, so `remote.local` did not resolve and admin/HTTPS was unavailable when launched via the installed service. The wrapper now reuses `run.py`'s `get_local_ip`/`setup_windows_firewall`/`start_mdns` helpers so the installed service and interactive launch take the same code path for these network bits. (Both `setup.py`'s install offer and `run.py --install` already delegate to `daemon.install()`, so the registered task itself is identical between them.)

## [2.1.1] — 2026-05-16
- **Bug fix:** qBittorrent no longer launches on startup when Mullvad VPN is off. `run.py` now checks VPN status before starting qBit; if VPN is down, qBit is skipped and the watchdog will start it once VPN connects.

## [2.1.0] — 2026-05-16
- **Minor feature:** Fullscreen vol − / + buttons now detect hold-down (≥400 ms) and apply a ±15 step instead of ±5; short taps retain the original ±5 behaviour. Repeats every 350 ms while held.

## [2.0.0] — baseline
- Initial versioned release (previously tracked as alpha1/alpha2).
